<Author>LukePerth
<Content>Our fourth visit to Balli In October my wife(56) and I (60) went to Sanur because we were looking for a very relaxed break. We got it; staying 12 nights at Bali Hyatt after failing to get our preference the recommended Puri Santrian and the resort beside it, the Sanur Beach. Primarily I'd have to say that the Bali Hyatt simply shouldn't be carrying that brand - the resort is too old and outdated. Nothing really compensates for the poor state of the brick and mortar (well, stone and tiles), the rattlng lift, the past-their-use-by date swimming pools. Hyatt should bulldoze the building and start again - but retain the magnificient gardens and ponds. The resort begs a new building and better beach facilities. We stayed at the ocean view rooms (make sure you get a king size bed for a couple), which are probably the best bet because of the view over the gardens to the ocean. We didn't inspect the club rooms but were told they were the same size with an inland view. An endearing and indelible feature was the high standard of cordiality of staff. Without exception every visitor got what seemed to be a genuine a smile and a good morning, every day, every time and excellent service. On reflection Nusa Dua probably offers a better, sunnier, more modern holiday; whereas Kuta is a party town.

<Author>DebNottingham
<Content>Beautiful Gardens Just returned from the Bali Hyatt Sanur, the gardens where spectacular, by far one of the nicest settings I have been to. We had a room in the Regency Club and would reccomend anybody to upgrade to this as its well worth the experience and money. Breakfast was an assortment of hot and cold foods, nothing was too much trouble and the service was excellent. They also offered you drinks daily between 5 and 7 along with a beautifull buffet. Drinks in the rest of the hotel were expensive along with the food. Outside the hotel there are many bars and restaurants offering some excellent food very cheaply.The beach was stunning, but if you want to swim in the sea, this is not the resort for you. The water is very shallow and only accesible to swimming if you take a boat out to the corral reef.The spa was well worth the visit, although not cheap, it was the most luxureous experience, would definately have gone again if had the time.Overall a fantastic hotel, a beautiful setting with excellent service.

We asked to move the next day which the hotel was happy to do. The rooms had everything we needed. The bed was huge with the most comfortable matress and pillows you could imagine. It was included in our pachage though it was normally 拢15 each, not sure it was worth that much (drinks not included) We ate at the beach restaurant out the hotel and turn right (beech side) it's the first one after you go through the barrier. Food was nice for lunch. Overall a nice hotel though could do with an update. If I went back to Sanur I would probably stay again.

<Author>Smooth_Sluggo
<Content>Nice, but not 5-star This is a beautiful hotel in a great location, with decent service and so-so rooms. If/when I travel to Bali I would definitely consider booking here again, but will look closer.The hotel grounds are beautiful. We stayed in a garden room with a stunning view of the lush gardens on the hotel grounds. If you like the night sounds of bugs and birds chirping, you will love tihs place. These rooms were also cheaper than the ocean view rooms, which, unlike the garden rooms, were not right on the ocean. The garden rooms were definitely a better value for the money.The rooms themselves are showing their age. Nice decorations and feel, but a tiny TV and an older bathroom are items you don't expect in a top resort. The one aspect of the hotel that was a real turn-off was the system of reserving beach and pool chairs with a towel. Its one thing if you're getting up to get a drink, but another when you're gone for several hours. I noticed a lot of people would do this, particularly on the beach where the number of chairs with shade is limited. I would hope that the hotel changes this policy in the future and limits the unoccupied time to 30 minutes--its simply not fair to the other guests.I was also disappointed when I left the hotel. Taxis are quite abundant in Sanur--just wait for 30 seconds and one will pass buy--and it was our intent to take one to the airport. The hotel first tried to sell us their shuttle (at 3x the price of a metered taxi), and then offered to call a taxi in using their service for 2x the price of the normal metered rate. It was only when we started to walk to the street that the offered to flag down a taxi. It was a shameless way to try and make a few extra dollars.Last gripe: what's up with not having an alarm clock in the room?

<Author>KMCP3122
<Content>Absolutely Beautiful! If you have been reading some of the other reviews below then all I can say is I completely agree with the littleherbets from Kent!On arrival we were greeted with a genuine smile, a refreshing drink and a welcomed cold towel! We were then shown to our room, a standard Garden View room, which was lovely. A huge bed and all the facilities you would require of your holiday room, including a hairdryer and excellent air conditioning! The rooms were tended to twice a day which included topping up supplies of free bottles of water, tea and coffee plus two lots of fresh towels as well as a high standard of cleaning.The hotel itself is beautiful. It is not your plastic fantastic hotel that you would get in the big cities but had been built to represent the traditional side of Bali, which we felt it captured completely. Both pools were lovely and there were more than enough sun beds to go around, even though the hotel was at capacity! You may have to get up a little earlier if you want a prime spot but if you don't feel like manoeuvring your own sun bed, the staff will do it for you. We ate in the hotel on the first night, for convenience more than anything else, which was delicious but is a lot more expensive than in the town. We then enjoyed meals out every night which ranged from 拢15 to 拢35. This was for 3 courses plus drinks so even the more costly meals were still excellent value for money!You can go either left or right out of the hotel to find ample restaurants There are more to the right but it's a bit more of a walk - unless you're feeling lazy and you get a taxi for 5000rph (approx 33p!) There is also a large supermarket to the right (Hardy's) or a smaller, closer one, to the left.We went on a couple of trips with Bali Tours, as they were in with the price of our holiday and we couldn't fault them. Again the staff were extremely friendly and also provided a very interesting and in-depth knowledge of the island and its history. The monkey temple was great as was Tannah Lot at sunset - beautiful!We did get a taxi to Kuta for a bit of a night out but it was not really our scene. It wasn't that we felt particularly unsafe (although stay on your guard, as you should on any night out!) but it was all dance music, which just gives me a headache! ;-)All in all Bali is an amazing island with amazing people and the Bali Hyatt complimented it very well! Enjoy x

<Author>saffier
<Content>beautiful gardens My husband and I booked a 10 night stay during which I celebrated my 40th birthday. Following a very long journey from the UK we finally arraived at the Hyatt to be greeted by the lovely smiling staff bearing lei garlands and cold fruit juice. Check in was easy and straight forward and then we were shown to our room- 2301, which overlooked the absolutely stunning gardens. We also had a huge sun terrace with 2 sun loungers and parasol in addition to the small patio table and chairs. There was no sign of dampness and the room was spotlessly clean. We had upgraded to the Regency Club and would recommend this. The Regency lounge is so peaceful and the perfect way to start the day with a gentle breakfast overlooking the pretty pond, watching the fish, dragonflys and occasional lizard. Its also very pleasant to go in there during the day for a cup of tea/coffee, and again early evening for a pre-dinner drink. I never experienced any problem obtaining a sun lounger. There were plenty of them available at least up to about 11am. My only slight critisism is that perhaps more parasols could be available as the palm trees didn't always provide enough shade- at least for my easily burnt, pale british skin!We ate quite a few times in the hotel and found prices to be reasonable, and the fish at the Oomang grill was delicious. Outside of the hotel there are plenty of cheaper restaurants; one of our favourites was the Bonsai Cafe a 20 minute walk north on the sea front promenade. However, we walked back along here one night and it was very dark as some of the overhead lights were not working so my advice would be to take a torch.We tried cheaper spa's outside of the hotel (Jari Menari in Seminyak is a must!) but the Wening massage in the Hyatt Spa just before bed was wonderfully relaxing and well worth the higher price. For two days we hired a driver who took us to the rice fields, temples, Ubud, Bali Bird and Reptile Park, a Barong show.....but Bali still has more to see than we could ever try to fit into 2 days. (The Bali forum on this website was invaluable in the planning of my trip)I have to admit that I was concerned by some of the negative reviews but all of these evaporated once we arrived. The staff couldn't have been more pleasant, helpful and genuinely friendly.We hope to make a return trip to Bali and have no hesitation in staying once more at the Hyatt.  
<Date>Oct 8, 2008

<Content>perfect After reading some reviews on trip advisor, i was hesitant to book at the bali hyatt but decided to just try it out as it looked better than the other options.i have to say that it was just incredible, me and partner were just in love with the place, it was so beautiful and everything looks just as it was in the photos.we booked a regency club room and were very pleased with it.breakfast:we got breakfast at the regency club and were impressed with the spread of fruit, breads, pastries, cereals, egss, traditional balinese breakfasts, juices and teas.. there was so much variety and the staff were so excellent, nothing was too much for them and they were all so so helpful and friendlywe did try breakfast at the wantilan cafe which we didnt find that different except that it was busy and that you have to toast your own bread and fill your own juice etc etcrooms:we had a regency club room which was nice and not too dissimilar to the the regular rooms except the bathrooms were a lot nicer. air condition worked lovely, rooms were kept very very clean, towels were changed regularly, and there were lots of channels on the tv. in short, it was everything you needed.hotel in general - <Author>AmandaChitown
<Content>Beautiful hotel in a great location Just returned from 4 nights at the Bali Hyatt and although I was hesitant to stay at a large chain hotel on such a unique island, I was very impressed with the location, atmosphere, security, staff and value of the Bali Hyatt. The pool area was great-2 pools plus a swim up bar, hot tub, cool tub, plenty of lounge chairs, ping pong and good poolside food and drinks. Hotel concierage was wonderful in booking us restaurant reservations, a driver to Ubud and a boating trip. (Take the Bali Hai Reef Cruise!). Service everywhere at the hotel was top notch. We did the Regency Club rate which included a great breakfast every morning and happy hour cocktails at night. The only complaint would be that the rooms were a little outdated but still decorated very nicely. It's not like you go to Bali to hang out in your hotel room anyways... The grounds were gorgeous and the beach is right out back. The ocean there is not the most ideal for swimming as it was mostly low tide when we saw it and didn't get much higher than your knees. Lots of great beach front huts nearby to get souvenirs and massages. The streets of Sanur are right out front and good local restaurants, bars and shops are within 5-10 min walk. Very easy to get taxis as well into Kuta or Seminyak, which are about 20-30 min away and $6-7 fare.

<Author>Tom28
<Content>Excellent service and a great place for a rest Just returned from a ten day stay at the Bali Hyatt and would recommend this place for anyone wanting excellent service and a restful holiday.We stayed in an ocean view room and were pleased with the room facilities. <Author>LiQ-American
<Content>County Club Feeling My wife and I had recently spent 4 days here after a stint at the Ritz, Bali. My idea not the wife's. We haven't stayed here since the summer of 2006. At that time, we left here very disappointed. The rooms were damp and dirty back then, and the service was somewhat lacking. Boy have things changed.  Upon our arrival, the manager from 2006 greeted us. He had all the details, (some of my negative feelings were listed) from our last visit 2 years ago, in fact from all our 3 previous visits at his hotel. This kind of freaked us out a bit. We had no need to worry. He was happy that we gave them another try. The first thing that he did was let us know that as soon as the Regancy Club room (which we were upgraded to), was ready, (4th floor over looking the ocean), we could settle in. Immediately I began to remind him that I heard that before at this hotel. He reassured us with 2 complimentary dinner vouchers for anything on the menu, while we waited for our room. That helped a bit for I had the steak sandwich.Great.  At about the time that we were finishing our meals, we were presented with our room card-keys, and were brought to the place we were to call home for the next 4 days. To say that we were knocked off our feet, would be an understatement. It was beautiful with a great view of the garden/lawn area and the ocean. An immediate amends from our disappointments of 2 summers ago, had been made. Of course this hotel doesn't come close in comparison to the Ritz or the Intercontinental resorts, but it has a great country club feel to it. They don't. People that had worked at the hotel and the beaches from 2 years ago, still remembered us. While the wife had a 2 hour spa at the hotel, I would go just beachside of the hotel to the right, and get my US$5.00 massage from Daimi. The same woman that took good care of the wife and I two years ago. The next day, while the wife had her hour long tennis lesson, I went sailing on a traditional Javanese sailboat with a buddy I ran into from 2 years ago named Madi. I think he stilll used the same boat from that time, for it looked a little worn. However, this added to the overall excitement and feel of our stay here. Sanur beach at high tide isn't very deep. In fact, it isn't over my head while swimming. So make sure that the tide is in, if you plan to do water sports. At low tide you could walk all the way to the reef. Maybe that's why some of the surfers that I ran into in Kuta call Sanur Beach, Sn-ore Beach. Keep the surfboards at home, if you are planning to stay at this hotel. The hotel food was very good with a reasonable price. The buffet breakfast had improved very much since our last stay. The buffet was served in an enclosed area, no flies/birds to contend with. Unlike 2 years ago, you weren't allowed to smoke in the buffet area. They did have a very nice area for me to smoke my Cohiba cigar in the morning, just outside and away from the decent folks in a separate windowed, but cool area. This made the wife very happy and free from embarrassment, and put me on display for other people to write about.. Kind of like being a monkey at a zoo. The hotel's Italian/pizza restaurant has a great selection. Also along the beach walkway you can find many quiet but perfect, eating establishments with both western and Balinese food and great views of the beach. All nice and very reasonably priced.  In conclusion, my wife said it wasn't the Ritz, but it was the best country club that we have joined and been members of in a very long time. A traditional Balinese feel in every area and every venue.  My wife was happy. I was happy. And to my surprise, my wallet was very happy with our overall stay at the Bali Hyatt in Sanur.*Note: Don't exchange your money here(very low rate). Go to the main road in front of the hotel and transact with the money changers there. Hey, not that I'm cheap,, but a nickel is a nickel in my book.

<Author>SpaceCadet01
<Content>Great location and comfortable stay After reading mixed reviews of the Bali Hyatt, my partner and I decided to book and to go with open minds, and we were pleasantly surprised by our stay.As a couple who would never usually go for a hotel that is part of such a large chain I was a little nervous about what to expect, but upon our arrival those fears melted away...We were greeted by polite staff and handed cold towels (which were a godsend!) along with fresh fruit juice, and the check in process was relatively quick and painless. We were give Lei's to wear which was fantastic for me but my partner found somewhat embarassing (there is photographic evidence obviously!). Also the staff take a photo of you when you arrive, which is left on your bed a few days later in a locally crafted frame (this is free of charge and a nice touch), but after a 22 hour journey it's possibly not the look you most want to remember!The rooms are situated in 3 'blocks', of 4 storeys high each, and my only real gripe about the hotel is the fact that in some places it does resemble a multi -storey carpark. I certainly wasn't expecting as much concrete as I found, although each block has a garden inside and at night they really do look quite pretty.This was howver the only real issue either of us had with the hotel. The room was clean and well decorated, and the amenties were as we would expect from a 4* hotel. The pools were lovely - especially the pool with the waterfall and the sand coloured base, which made it look like a natural lagoon (aside from all the right angles!). The beach was lovely and cleaned often, and the security gaurds did a fanticatic job of keeping non-residents out to ensure a blissfully relaxing time was had by all. There should be more umbrellas on the beach, as it was normally a race to get one in the morning despite it being low season, but aside from that it's great, and the reef makes for a great walk when the tide is out.We didn't eat in the hotel a huge amount so I don't feel suitably qualified to comment on the food, but the 3 lunchtime meals we had were lovely. The location is such that there really is no need to stay in the hotel and eat/drink. There are so many restaurants within walking distance, or a short Bemo ride (which costs 3000 Rupiah to get from one end of Sanur to the other, around 20p!). The hotel is expensive by Balinese standards (although not by the standards of international hotels). A small Bintang in the hotel cost 38,000 Rupiah after tax, but if you walk 2 minutes out the front of the hotel to a local bar/restuarant you'll pay between 10,000  16,000. All in all the hotel really was nice. The gardens were lovely, the pools were clean, the staff were freindly and helpful, and the location was absolutely perfect. the wildlife in the hotel grounds also makes for a memorable stay!Balinese people really are as fantastic as all the reviews you'll read, so if you can handle 2 weeks of 'LOOK IN MY SHOP' you'll no doubt have an absolutely amazing time, as we did!

<Author>Jayn
<Content>Best Hotel in Sanur We stayed at the Bali Hyatt for 12 nights in April. The hotel itself was great, the staff were lovely, and the gardens were amazing. The two pools were nice although the sun beds around the pools were taken quite early, however there were enough beds to sit in the gardens or on the beach which was a lot quieter. The breakfast was lovely, filtered coffee and lots of choice. We used room service a few times which was good and the prices were not too expensive although it is a lot cheaper to eat outside the hotel. The rooms were lovely although we had read the rooms were tired (not the case with ours at all). We had an ocean view room and our room was lovely. The pillows and king size bed were so comfortable and the towels were big and thick. The sink plug hole did occasionally smell but that wasn鈥檛 really a problem. The room was not humid as you have a machine in the room to control this. The spa is nice but very expensive compared to outside the hotel. If you like a nice hotel and you do want to visit Bali and Sanur then this hotel is really traditional and pretty.We ate out at a place called 'The Village' a few times and this cost about 拢20 for two people in total (more expensive than the other restaurants we went to) but is the nicest looking restaurant in Sanur just past Hardy's supermarket. We expected Sanur to be quiet, but not as quiet as it was. We were going in about 10pm most nights after our meal as there aren't many bars at all. Sometimes it felt like we were the only tourists walking back to our hotel. The people are friendly and not once did we feel unsafe even when we went to Kuta for a few hours. The weather was fantastic; I think we only had 10 mins of rain in 12 days. This was our first trip to Bali and even though we loved this hotel if you go beyond the beach outside the Bali Hyatt it isn鈥檛 very nice, it was quite disappointing. The beach at the hotel is lovely but the sea is full of seaweed and not very inviting considering you are in the Indian Ocean. The beach to the left and right of the hotel isn鈥檛 very nice. There are stalls/shops either side of the hotel and you do get asked a number of times if you want transport or a massage and the rubbish on the beaches outside these stalls is not very nice. If you are expecting paradise when you go to Bali I think you maybe a bit disappointed. We thought the country itself was pretty and green when we travelled outside the hotel to see the Rice Fields and moutains etc but they should really keep the beaches tidy as that was a total put off, you do not see or hear about this so just be aware. We visited the sister hotel (Grand Hyatt) at Nusa Dua and even though this hotel was new and fantastic, once you walk along the lovely beach in Nusa Dusa we came across flip flops, corn on a cob and loads of empty crisp packets etc. Not our idea of paradise I am afraid. I just think it would not take much to keep on top of these beaches. I appreciate it is a third world country and we have been to a lot of places including India and Thailand but haven鈥檛 experienced rubbish on the beach like this before. But if you are happy to stay in the hotel grounds then this is a lovely hotel although expensive to eat and drink in compared to eating outside.

<Author>wood97
<Content>Good choice Stayed here for 9 days with my family . We all liked the hotel and the grounds/gardens were absolutely first rate as were the pools. Staff all very friendly as well.The location was good - you can walk out and along the beach front to find plenty of local facilities, or along the road in either direction. Within the hotel there are various options to eat, all pretty good standard. The buffet breakfast is absolutely superb with something for everyone.As for the rooms, I read many reports on this website of the rooms being poor standard/damp/dated and so on, but its hard to understand where these people are coming from. We found the rooms to be of good standard with very efficient a/c, comfortable beds, good standard bathrooms plus a balcony.We booked 2 rooms next to each other which were separate but had a shared entrance lobby by the clever use of an extra set of double doors thus creating an interconnecting double room set up. The hotel has a 'family plan' where you get the second room at half rate. This made the hotel reasonably affordable for us and although the incidentals are not cheap compared to local standards, they arent too bad by international hotel standards.You can arrange tours via the hotel but if you take the trouble to step out of the hotel you can hire a car plus driver to take you anywhere you might wish to visit at very reasonable rates - do negotiate though.One word of caution. beware the territorial beach towel behaviour of folks from certain European countries. They seem to nab all the best slots by the pools VERY early (I suspect they might be bribing the pool attendants to do this on their behalf the night before). We found this only to be a problem at peak time (morning) whereas if you look for a place in the afternoon you can generally find one. In my opinion this sort of thing should not be allowed by the hotel as most of the sun beds were reserved but no sign of anyone whatsoever for hours on end. I guess you get this problem everywhere in the world these days. Having said all that its such a huge hotel you can always find somewhere - for example the beach beds were mostly vacant.Try the shuttle to the Grand Hyatt for a change of scene. Its a fairly pleasant place with big facilities. It's a newer hotel but lacking the pleasant ambience of the Sanur hotel.If you have young kids, a trip to the monkey forest is a laugh (our 7 year old had his hat pinched which caused much amusement) and it's a fairly short trip out. Also Kuta has to be seen and the Waterbom park is a good trip to do with children.  
<Date>Apr 24, 2008

<Author>Bopa
<Content>Lovely time at the Bali Hyatt Just returned from a lovely stay at the Bali Hyatt. I must say after reading some reviews I was a little worried about some comments that have been made. I needn't have been from the moment we arrived until the day we left I really don't have anything major to complain about.Our room was just great. It was in hibiscus block which is the first block from reception. We were on the top floor in an ocean view room and had a lovely view to the beach and the gardens. If you want a large balcony I suggest a lower floor as the building slopes and the balconies get narrower as you get to the top.Our room was serviced twice a day. Clean towels added each time. We had no complaints at all. The man who cleaned the room knew our names and when I asked for extra detergent a few packets were added to the room straight away and was kept that way until we left.Staff were very friendly and helpful especially around the pool and beach area. Every morning there was someone willing to help us find a bed for on the beach and put it just where we wanted. The beach was kept clean at all times especially after the rain when it was cleared of debris etc. We wanted a relaxing holiday in a nice location and really think this was achieved at the Bali Hyatt. We visited Kuta mainly for shopping and I must say it was so good to get back to the hotel for peace and quiet. Kuta is ok for a visit and shopping but be warned it is a really busy place. Lots of people trying to get you into their stores to buy and the beach is not a patch on Sanur.If I return to Bali the Bali Hyatt would be my number one choice.On our last day we asked to keep our room until 3pm as we were leaving at 4pm and this wasn't a problem and made life easier for us as we were able to shower and relax before our long journey back to the UK.

<Author>lhotse
<Content>Nice Play To Stay We stayed at the Bali Hyatt Sanur Beach for 3 nights in early March. It was a rather last minute decision to book at this hotel so I know I did not get the best rate for our ocean view standard room, but still, it wasn't totally over the top ($140 for the Sunday night, then $175/nt for Mon and Tues night). Our rate included a breakfast buffet which was plentiful and very tasty. The hotel grounds are quite lovely with two pools and access to the beach. If you are looking for a swimming beach however, I don't think the beach in the back of the hotel is ideal. I would describe it more as a beach to sunbathe on or to splash around in. That was a bit disappointing to my boyfriend who enjoys swimming in the ocean. Our room, though a little old in appearance, was comfy. I liked the location of the hotel because we were able to walk to many shops and very good restaurants (we highly recommend Massimo's if you need a break from Indonesian food and want some delicious Italian at cheap prices). As with most Balinese hotels, the service was excellent at the Hyatt. I don't know if we'd book here again in the future but we did enjoy our stay.

<Author>philippeenrique
<Content>Terrible hotel - concrete and waste of time After having stayed at the Maya Ubud, we were supposed to stay at the Bali Hyatt for ten days. As soon as we arrived and discovered this monster of concrete, we already had doubts that we would have fun here. And unfortunately, we could not stand it. Bali Hyatt is presumably the oldest hotel in Bali, according to what we heard, typical 70s style, and is known to be of very mediocre quality. The rooms are tiny. The ceiling is low, there is a labyrynth of stairs and concrete with very old vegetation that may have covered it in the past but does not do its job anymore. Worse of all is the fact that from 1pm, the sea disappears. You have to walk for several dozens meters to be able to wet your toes in a dirty water.Seriously, it's a hotel to be avoided as much as possible.It's useless to go to Asia and get this poor level of service. We can have this in Europe, without travelling!!!After one night, we moved out to the Intercontinental, which fulfilled all our expectations, but that's another story, I suppose.Philippe from Paris

<Author>mrsweston2b
<Content>heaven at the Bali Hyatt We stayed at the Bali Hyatt for 5 nights as part of our honeymoon in Asia and we had a fantastic time. I was a little concerned after reading negetive reviews about the hotel but after staying there I realy cannot understand why people can write anything negetive about this wonderful hotel!We arrived after a short flight from Singapore and the welcome we received was unlike any welcome I have ever received at any hotel before. the staff sat us down and made us feel at home with a lovely cocktail and a flower garland. We arrived quite early and our room was not ready as we had booked a sea view but we were happy to sit by the pool until our room was ready which was 4pm. The room itself was a good size with a lovely view of the gardens and sea and although a little musty this was understandable because of the humidity.The pool area at the hotel was beautiful and the staff were fantastic. I can't understand why people complain about the pices at the hotel. we ate luch 4 times, dinner twice and had drinks by the pool every day (happy hour at the pool bar!) and our bill was only 拢120 for the two of us at the end of the holiday which we thought was fantastic in comparison to European prices. Fair enough it was more expensive that the resort restaurants but was worth it for the convenience.Restaurants in resort were fantastic and so cheap! We booked a driver for 2 days (Dean) who was fabulous and we got the chance to see the 'Real' Bali by doing this which was worth every penny.We can't praise this hotel enough and we can't wait to go back. we did venture out to Kuta but felt it was little built up but was great for a night out and shopping. Sanur was perfect for us though.

<Author>Paulgr
<Content>A big hotel that still feels personal. For our second stay in Sanur we decided to go a little upmarket so picked the Hyatt as it is about in the middle of Sanur Beach. Right from the start the experience was first class. Smiling greeting, frangipani leis, welcome drink and immediate check in and access to the room despite it being 9am! Thank you!!We had ground floor, beach front in Bougainvillea Court - furthest from reception but closest to the beach - 40 metres from our french doors to the sun lounges on the sand. You could see the breaker line on the lagoon's reef without lifting your head off the king bed's pillows. Bliss.Hyatt make the place feel like a smaller hotel by having the same staff member assigned to your area - same guy cleans every day, (different but) same guy replaces your used towels and turns your bed down in the evening, same gardiner out the front. All smiling. Offering fresh towels twice in the day is a good touch in the tropics, too. We are looking forward to staying again.TIP! Join Hyatt's Gold Passport before staying for extra benefits like free room service morning coffee.

<Author>discovery204
<Content>Tranquil and Beautiful sums up the Bali Hyatt We stayed in the Bali Hyatt over Chinese New Year in February and loved it. The gardens are beautiful and resplendent with wonderful birds, squirrels, fish and lizards. It really seems to be a peaceful and natural spot. The rooms were up to standard in a 5* hotel, we had a big balcony and views over the gardens. The fruit bowl was replenished daily with lovely tropical friuts and complimentary water. The rooms were cleaned twice a day and towels replaced reguarly. Yes, the bathrooms are a little old and the toilet position a bit strange but clean and useable. The air-con was a little hot for us even on the lowest setting. We had a top floor room and never heard any noise from other rooms or guests. Everything we asked for in our booking was provided - connecting and non smoking rooms. We greatly enjoyed the Recency Club, with free daily tea and coffee and nibbles and cocktails from 5-7pm. The service in the club was wonderful and the ambience relaxing. Our boys enjoyed the food there and the drinks. The other restaurants in the hotel were good, we enjoyed the spectacular breakfasat buffet at the Wantilan Cafe, the Italian resturant and the Wednesday buffet evening meal with a traditional Balinese dance performance. The dance was very impressive! The restaurants outside are of course cheaper but beware the ones that use MSG in quantity in their cooking! The exception was the excellent Italian Restaurant 5 mins walk left as you turn out of the hotel. This served great food, at a good cost with no MSG - watch out for the impressive range of ice creams at the stand at the entrance. Our only slight gripe about the restaurants in the hotel (and the Italian up the road) were the small non-smoking areas. Being non-smokers we found the hotel and Bali in general had very few areas for non-smokers to enjoy fresh air. The Wantilan Cafe smoking tables were far better situated than the non-smoking tables and the hotel seemed to have loads of smoking guests when we were there. The hotel had good facilities, including the fabulous swimming pool areas and beach. We also enjoyed the badminton court and the bikes - cycling along the beach path was enjoyable and easy. Its a shame that the hotel imposes small charges on facilities, many other 5* hotels provide these for free. Try to get to the Waterbom park at Kuta (go by taxi) if you have children, they will love the water slides and book yourself a pagoda for the day to relax in with shade. We also enjoyed a tour to Lembongan island with Bali Hai tours and a look at the area around Ubud. We will certainly reurn to Bali, there is so much to do, but next time we will be sure to bring US DOLLARS as well as Rupiah as so much is charged in US $ and the exchange rate is much better at home than in Bali.

<Author>ziutka
<Content>Harsh beginning We ordered transport from Denpasar's airport to the hotel through their website. There was additional $8 charge for the service even though most of cheaper hotels with less * usually provide it free of charge. Well, it is not a lot of money, but it gives very bad impression. The impression became even worse when we realised that nobody was there to pick us up. We took a regular taxi to the hotel and asked them at the counter what had happened. The senior (?) manager told us that we were suppose to arrive in an earlier flight and presented a paper with a note for their drivers. We had a printed confirmation with all the flight data, verifying that we informed them about our actual arrival. So, it was obvious someone made a mistake on their side. The man several times repeated he has to check it first and because it was already around 2:00 am, he suggested us to check in and contact them the following day. Nobody even said sorry and despite the fact we had a proof of the hotel's error, they insisted us to contact them. Of course we voiced out and told the man that they should contact us to clarify the whole thing, not the other way. I also asked him how it is possible that nobody even apologised - and there was no reaction other then a smile and nod of the head. It took them two days before they were able to verbalize the apology, moreover it was quite strained...One thing they did correct was to offer us the transport back to the airport for free. Despite this harsh startup I have to tell that overall service was good there. All the people smiling, efficient, quick and patient room service, courteous waiters etc. The whole hotel is old and requires renovation. Being honest I think it is a little bit overpriced for such relatively low quality. We had the King Ocean View room and the bathroom tiles were terrible (old, not really clean), bathtub quite rusty, everything very used, slightly too loud aircondition, tv volume control not working at times etc. The breakfast at Regency Club was rather chaste (nice ambience though), but the one in Wantilan Restaurant offered really good choices with a mixture of local and continental food. Speaking/writing about the food... We ate one dinner in Pizza Ria and one more in the BBQ bar before we decided to go outside the hotel for the following evenings looking for better options. The appetizers were good in both places, big sized :) and tasty. The main courses were not satysfying, frankly speaking. Average, as it happens quite often in a hotels. We really liked the surroundings, gardens etc. of the hotel, including adorable squirrels.

<Author>Montza
<Content>Really relaxing place, great facilities, perfect for families We stayed at the Bali Hyatt in October 2007 for 7 nights. We had a Ocean King Room and in our package was the usual breakfast inclusion. It was the end of Ramadan so Bali was BUSY BUSY BUSY with domestic and international tourists. We normally stay in Legian or Seminyak and were a little apprehensive at first about staying in Sanur, but not spoilt for choice given we planned our trip on short-notice - away we went.As with a lot of flights into Bali, we arrived very late in the evening and were very impressed with the check-in facilities even at 1am, our room was ready as expected and we set off to the room with a hotel staffer. The Hyatt is set over 3 large 'blocks' or units. They are each built around lovely gardens and room entries are from the centre of the block enabling the rooms to look out over either the beach / resort or gardens.The room was a little tired, we've read other reviews on TripAdvisor before about the hotel being Tired so we thought best to try and define what we mean by this. The bathrooms have not been updated since new, they were gorgeous in design and represented the quality of fittings when they were built, but could do with a few modern touches. The bed, whilst comfortable, was clearly due for replacement - it was an older spring style mattress, the room could have done with a paint job too. Of our experience, our room was the only thing we were not entirely satisfied with.The hotel facilities are amazing. Absolutely sensational. The breakfast is served in a traditional open air dining room. Being a large hotel, it is a very large facility. Guests had a choice to have breakfast in the main dining area or alternatively at a more boutique terrace style setting just neighboring the main area. The buffet was amazing with a true global array of breakfasts including local South East Asian, Japanese, American and European. Certainly suggest not sleeping in, although where most hotels are 'to the minute' strict on breakfast, we were running late a number of mornings and there was never a question asked.The pool is stunning. It is quite picturesque with gorgeous stone structures of Indonesian cultural symbols. With overhead trees dropping Frangipanis into the pool it was really a special setting. Plenty of space with lap swimming as well as a just relaxing in the pool. There was also a hot tub / jacuzzi and cold plunge which provided a great break from the normal pool. Guests can use banana lounges either around the pool or throughout the grass area that fronts onto the beach, you can also get a lounge with umbrella on the beach, although a late breakfast meant we missed out on those most days.We went running, jet skiing, snorkeling, bike riding, glass bottom boat as our activities through the hotel. Suprisingly activities booked through the hotel were reasonably priced vs. the hawkers operating outside the resort - if you didn't want to bargain and haggle you were not getting ripped off through the hotel - quite refreshing actually!Running was a clear highlight and made a pleasure from the hotels beach-front location. There is a great track along the Sanur beach-front which was perfect for running. I managed to get out each morning for a jog before it got too hot (generally before 9am). If you're keen to combine exercise with your holiday and not just laze around all day, you'll enjoy this aspect.We dined at the poolside restaurant one night, which was enjoyable, but being Bali regulars we went to our regular restaurants and some new ones including La Lucciola in Seminyak, Teras in Legian and of course Cafe Melasti at Jimbaran Bay. We found a very nice Italian restaurant in Sanur about 5 minutes walk from the hotel, the name slips my mind for now, apologies, there look to be a lot of great restaurants in the main Sanur 'shopping' area - get out and about.Finally, we went as a couple, however there were a number of families there. The kids looked to have an absolute ball, there were lots of kids activities and the staff looked to genuinely know what they were doing. We never heard kids crying poolside once - refreshing, but says something about how enjoyable it must have been for them (not to mention mum and dad!).

<Content>Fit like an old shoe Comfortable rooms, great service and facilities but due for a freshen up.I spent 9 days in Bali with my wife and two boys for a wedding and stayed the whole time at the Bali Hyatt. We all enjoyed it and I recommend it to others.We had adjoining rooms with a garden view. The rooms were comfortable and clean with tiled floors.The bathrooms were a bit small - if you are a tall person you might actually find it difficult getting on and off the toilet (see the photos from other visitors on this site).Our package included breakfast for the whole stay. The food was great quality and plentiful. I highly recommend the fresh made waffles.We also ate at the Italian restaurant 'Pizza Ria. We were pleasantly surprised by the quality of the food there. Other than breakfast we didn't eat in the hotel much as the food is much cheaper, and generally more interesting at the local restaurants.The staff were all very pleasant and the service was great.Our only disappointment was the laundry service - they did not really get our clothes clean.If you have kids keep an eye out for the wild life. There are native squirrels in the trees and lots of frogs of all sizes. There are also insects of all sizes in the gardens - we never saw any in our room.Yes, as others have said is that that hotel is showing its age a bit . It just looks old. But we were very happy and comfortable.  
<Date>Feb 1, 2008

<Author>ChrisfromPerth
<Content>Love the Bali Hyatt I absolutely loved it - the 3rd time I've stayed at the Bali Hyatt. I have read some reviews that are critical of the hotel needing updating and yes, not everything is as perfect as you'd find in a 5 star city hotel. The climate takes its toll and things fall apart faster than you might expect. Yes, it's humid (blame the tropics). The woodwork could do with refinishing. Some of the tiles look a bit jaded, especially outdoors. But my rooms were very clean and well serviced, the bathrooms were scrubbed on a daily basis. What you'll find at the Bali Hyatt are: marvelous public facilities, friendly service, great food and drinks, wonderful pools, clean well-serviced rooms, glorious tropical gardens. We were treated like royalty (probably because we're repeat customers). If you join the Regency Club those facilities are also excellent (essentially breakfasts, complimentary tea/coffee all day and cocktails/canapes each evening in a private luxury setting). Very child-friendly and even my kids were made to feel special. I'm planning to return.

<Author>catz21
<Content>Way behind the Competition! We stayed at 4 (4 and 5 star) hotels whilst in Bali and as a Hyatt Gold Passport Holder we found it not just lacking against Bali standards it was lacking against the Hyatt service standards as well. Not only is the hotel screaming to be renovated it was the small things that continuously let in downWe actually treated ourselves at the Hyatt and opted for a Suite over the New Year Period and although in its day I am sure it was a splender it is has never been updated. The walls still had the original cement render pattern that was very popular way back when and floor tiling not only in the bathroom but in the entire suite was crying to be regrouted. The 3 mouse traps of a cardboard square, oil and dried fish (dont worry they where checked daily!) was of great amusement and to be honest if we hadnt prepaid we would have checked out and found elsewhere. I have to say there definitely was no damp smell within the suite and the aircon worked well - however I can see how it could be an issue as there was a strong damp smell when walking through certain areas of the hotel.Within 3 hours of check-in we had a strange phonecall from a local with a made up story about having already driven for us at the airport on the 24th of Dec (quite suspicious as considering we arrived on the 19th and had transport through the Intercontinental) asking if his services where needed (again??). He had our full names and room number and after a little bit of research I am sure our details had been passed out from a Hyatt staff member. The Irony of this is that we had suits made from a well known and reputable tailor in which the Hyatt not only refused to put their phonecall through they also failed to pass on the message!!! The Regency club staff where great and pre-dinner drinks in the club was a casual but lovely affair, breakfast itself in the club is good however the first morning order was taken and forgotten - genuine mistake and forgiven however this set the pattern of those little things building up to becoming a genuine complaint.The Pizza Ria was great and ended up eating there 3 times however they did mess up the order and gave my pizza to another table in which I had to wait an extra 15 minutes whilst my partner was eating his, the other visits in the restaurant where an extra ingredient was requested was also never followed through. The main breakfast area had a great buffet with chefs on hand to cook eggs to your liking, take note though make sure someone stays at the table at all times because you will lose it. In the space of popping up to grab a pastry (another coffee was on order) our table was being cleaned for reseating (3 people cleaning with people waiting to be sat down). As you can see the little things are starting to build up.We had room service which arrived promptly and hot however the requested side condiments did not arrive at all - forgivable ....... absolutely as it does happen and normally wouldn't even suffice a mention in any review however due to the constant mishap it definitely landed on the radar with us this time.Even Check out wasn't a smooth affair, With the pattern of mistakes occurring and now our distrust of Bali Hyatts attention to detail we decided to request a itemised bill early to ensure that it was correct, and Yep you guessed it ..............there where charges on the bill that had came from another room. Once the Hyatt staff requested the invoice copies from Room Service the mistake was acknowledged and rectified ( the process did take just under 45 minutes though). Overall though we loved Sanur and will seek to stay in the area again - Just not at the Hyatt!

<Author>C-RonSanFrancisco
<Content>Didn't like the Bali Hyatt I had high hopes for the Bali Hyatt since it's highlighted in several books for its uniquely Balinese landscaping, but I was very disappointed in the place, especially in comparison to the other comparable places we stayed in Bali. Here's what I disliked: 1. The rooms were very dated, from the yellowing tub to the past-their-prime tiles. 2. Our non-smoking room smelled like smoke. 3. The pools were really crowded. 4. They had trouble patching phone calls to our room so we couldn't connect with our friends. 5. They charge crazy prices for amenties, drinks, food and anything extra they can squeeze out of you - they charged me $6 for 30 minutes of internet use, which is just rediculous! 6. The staff is not very helpful, and they foist their expensive car service on you when you ask them to call you a taxi (which is like 3 times more expensive than a taxi - you have to specifically ask for, and insist on, a metered taxi if you want one. They won't even give you the option of one, which is lame.)We had rooms of similar price at the Conrad in Nusa Dua and Sofitel in Seminyak, but those rooms were way more spacious, everything was updated and/or new, the resorts were a lot less crowded, they had nice amenities (such as feather beds and comforters) and the staff was way more attentive and helpful, and those resorts never nickled and dimed us like the Bali Hyatt did. Compared to the other places we stayed, the Bali Hyatt was a huge disappointment.There were tons of families there, so maybe it's a good place for people travelling with kids, but for people searching for a peaceful and plush Bali getaway or a great deal, this isn't it.

<Content>Beautiful Bali Hyatt We stayed in the Bali Hyatt in Sanur as part of our honeymoon. <Author>Bakesey
<Content>Absolutely Fantastic We stayed at the Bali Hyatt end of September and it was absolutely magical!The hotel feels totally original (not like the huge corporate hotels in Nusa Dua) and has its own soul.From the moment you arrive at the Hyatt you know that you've made the right choice.The gardens are magnificent and the Koi lakes amazing.Both swimming pools looked gorgeous and clean but, to be honest we spent every day on the beach - no shortage of beach loungers and you are kept cool by the sea breezes.After a huge breakfast every morning - made to order eggs, bacon sausage etc together with delicious pastries, do nuts and waffles, we skipped lunch most days.Even though the food in the hotel is I'm sure lovely (only ate in on the first night!) walk into Sanur town (left or right) and you can eat in a different place EVERY night for 2 weeks. Chicken Satay  Nasi Goreng particular favourites of mind. Try the many Indian restaurants as well as they are very good. Budget for about 拢5 for 2 people including beers - yes, it really us that cheap!!Take an empty suitcase with you as gifts and souvenirs are SOOO cheap you won't have any problems filling the case!The Balinese shopkeepers love bartering and you can usually get goods for about 50% of the starting price.For you smokers out there, 200 cigarettes cost about 拢3.50!!!A wonderful place, we will definately go back to the Bali Hyatt in Sanur.

<Author>sammc
<Content>Rooms let it down, but lovely overall We had a lovely two weeks in Bali and stayed at the Hyatt. We wanted a relaxing escape for two weeks and that's what we got. When I arrived after over 20 hours travelling I was a bit disappointed. They left us hanging around a bit to be shown to our rooms. And the room was dated - terracotta tiles which reminded me of a spanish apartment and dated furniture. The bathroom was particularly outdated. BUT we ended up having a great time in the Bali Hyatt.The pools are lovely and the sunbeds, towels etc are very nice. The staff were good and unlike some Asian hotels I've stayed in didn't seem to expect tips all the time. There is a service charge on everything anyway.The food was great and while more expensive than outside the hotel, it was pretty good value. They make their own bread in the hotel and it was great. Really enjoyed the lunches there but opted to go elsewhere in the evenings.The gardens are great. Staff were very attentive to our room. The sheets were crisp and clean, the bed was huge and comfortable and the air conditioning worked well. There was a great selection of TV channels too.We did have a cockroach problem in the bathroom (they were small cockroaches thankfully) and the hotel dealt quickly with this.In my view the rooms are 3 star, the complex is 4 star, the food and service close to 5 star. So overall it gets away with its four star rating.It's best point is its location. Lots of bars and restaurants around. and we didn't want to be stuck in a hotel for two weeks. If you're looking for a very luxurious hotel, this mightn't be for you, but its a good standard and very pleasant place to stay in

<Author>Londoner-Couple
<Content>Highly recommended A breakdown:the rooms - 3starthe lobby and grounds - 4starthe staff - 5starOverall - 4star.This hotel is great. Went for a 1 week stay and loved it. There's 3 towns most tourist stay in - Nusa Dua, Kuta or Sanur. Nusa Dua is a huge complex made up of lots of 4  5 star hotels. It is all very new, but every hotel is virtually identical. Its a very standardised, americanised area where you don't get a feel of the real Bali. It is worth noting that the beaches here are terrible compared to Kuta or Sanur. However, the hotels are stunning and that is what you pay for. Kuta on the other hand is a slightly low class affair. While the beach is definitely better than Nusa Dua, the town itself is populated with tourists all looking for fake designer labels which lends it a rather low rent feel. The Bali Hyatt is based in Sanur. This is definitely the quietest tourist area, with much cheaper restaurants in the local area, and also a more relaxed feel. We were impressed when we arrived, but rather less so with the rooms. We stayed in a standard room, and although adequate, I imagine the hotels in Nusa Dua would blow these rooms away. Having said that, you shouldn't go to Bali and spend all day in your room anyway. The start of the day commences with fabulous buffet in the Wantilan Cafe, where everything from made-to-order omellettes, to fresh fruits, to traditonal indonesian breakfast items (noodles etc). Then you chill out by the pools or beach. The pools at this hotel were good but the ones at the Grand Hyatt in Nusa Dua are amazing.Finally, the staff at the Bali Hyatt deserve mention. I would say 90% of the staff greet you as you walk past them. It really is that friendly. When we visited the hotels in Nusa Dua, I would say less than 10% of the staff greeted us. And there in a nutshell is why you go to the Balu Hyatt. It may not be as new as Nusa Dua but the beach and service is better, and the only things Kuta offers is a better beach(i.e. more waves) though much,much, much more crowded beach and a wealth of fake-designer stores.

<Author>Ringraider
<Content>Fantastic hotel! I have just returned from 9 nights at the Hyatt and wish I was still there!This is probably the best hotel I have ever stayed in, in terms of how much I enjoyed my stay - I travel regularly for work and often stay in well-rated and expensive hotels, albeit usually in cities rather than resorts.It would be impossible to run an operation like this in the West. The time and care thast goes into everything is incredible - people are continually clearing up, sweeping sand off the path, clearing up leaves from the gardens, etc. Take a wander up the beach beyond the hotel and it will dawn on you that the beach isn't like that the whole way up; rather, it is immaculately maintained by the hotel staff. Hence, if you stay elsewhere in Sanur you will probably have a much less nice bit of beach in front of your hotel or villa.We stayed in an Ocean View room in Bougainvillea Court, the nearest of the 3 blocks to the sea. It was nice to have the view but all rooms have balconies or terraces and the gardens are so beautiful that the Garden View rooms are no doubt very pleasant too. The hotel was built in the early seventies, since which time hotel design has probably moved on a bit, but the rooms are large and pleasant with a bit of character from the Balinese furniture. I also liked the bathroom - not brand new in gleaming marble but quite attractive.The bed was massive and very comfortable, with quality bed linen that is changed very frequently. The minibar prices were pretty reasonable and for a change we made quite a bit of use of it.The hotel restaurants are good - in particular the fish from the Omang Grill. The Chinese restaurant is also excellent, an open-sided pavillion in a lily pond that serves more interesting food than the usual sweet and sour, beef in black bean sauce etc. Both are expensive compared to restaurants in the village but it is only relative; the proces are styill pretty cheap by European and in particular UK prices, especially for the setting and quality.Breakfast is served in the Wantilan Cafe - this is modelled on the temple meeting halls of the same name and is a large, open-sided timber building with a grass roof. It was wonderful to have your breakfast in the sun, alongside the ponds, overlooking the beautiful gardens. There is a full range of food available, from fresh fruits, good breads, pastries and yoghurts to Asian choices (looked nice enough but not for breakfast, thanks) to a Fatty Counter for the Anglo/Saxon contingent (US, UK, German), serving eggs, bacon, waffles etc.We made use of the spa one afternoon, not cheap in local terms but pretty good value compared to the UK and again you would not find something with a comparable setting - beautiful private villas for the treatments with gardern showers, pools etc.The best thing about the hotel, though, is probably the gardens, which really are amazing. They surround the hotel and make the areas around the pools very attractive, as well as providing a bit of shade. They also soften or hide the hotel buildings quite effectively; time has not been too kind to the 1970s concrete and whilst the inside of the hotel is all very nice the concrete has deteriorated quite a bit on the outside. This would look desperate if the hotel were in somewhere like Greece or Spain, where it is drier and the vegtation usually a bit more sparse, but here you don't really notice as the buildings melt into the trees.A word should also be said about the staff, who are a real credit to the hotel. They are unfailingly helpful and friendly.For recommendations outside the hotel:Turning right out of the gate and walking up Jalan Danau Tamblingan, try LUMUT on the left for dinner. This is a beatiful restaurant on top of a shop and gallery. Very stlyish Balinese decor and great presentation. Slightly more expensive than aomwe of the lowest common denominator tourist places but a cut above (and still very reasonable).CAFE BATUJIMBAR is a very stylish cafe on the right, great for coffee (try the Balinese rather than the Lavazza) and lunch, and has a good deli attached.

<Author>JandGCoppull_Lancs
<Content>Heaven on earth We stayed at the hyatt as part of a twin centre holiday which was amazing. First we visited buzzing Hong Kong which was fab but not really a holiday as just so much to see and do, so we were ready to relax when we got to Bali.The hotel is beautiful we had booked a sea view room which was well worth it the view was breathtaking. The gardens in the hotel are also beautiful.Staff pleasant and helpful, we stayed bed and breakfast (breakfast excellent lots of choice) BB is all you need, if you wish to sample the local restaurants and experience some of the culture.My partner loves diving so he went diving which he booked over there with a lady called Camilla at a loal diving school. She was great involved me aswell and I was just a spectator on the boat! who did a litlle snorkelling which was fab!The best trip we did whilst we were there was the Elephant Safari if your going you must do this but becareful make sure you go to the original park as there are two parks, the original one was opened by a man who rescue's elephants from Sumatra and brings elephant keepers with them who really do care for the elephants. This one is a good hour away but you pass all the beautiful rice fields which look like green waterfalls on the way and you see the volcano in the distance too plus you get to see some of the local villages. Apparently somebody has tried to copy this park and opened another one which is not meant to be as good.Jimbaran bay is the best place to go and watch the sunset lots ofseafood restaurants on the beach and you can choose your fish and have it freshly cooked to order. Even worth a try if your not seafood lovers we didn't think we would like it but it was delicious and the setting very romantic! (Red Snapper, Tiger Prawns, Clams, Rice, Salad, Sauces 拢8 in total and enough food really for 4 people and there were only two of us). Jimbaran bay is about 20mins away in a taxi but make sure you book a taxi to pick you up we didn't and ended up getting a lift back with a local man! Luckily he was nice and didn't rip us off but not really recommended!In Sanur there are lots of nice places to eat, Lazar bar for good steaks, Cat  Fiddle was a good irish pub also serves good food, but we never had a bad meal anywhere and itsjust embarassingly cheap. 3 courses for 2 people plus 3 rounds of drinks averaged at about 拢25 - 拢30.You must have a balinese massage whilst your there the hotel spa is excellent.Enjoy!!!

<Author>anna333
<Content>go for it!! Don't hesitate, book it. Indeed some reviews were not so inviting so I thought twice about booking the Bali Hyatt. We stayed 10 days and really loved our stay there as someone said already any negatives at Bali Hyatt are vastly outweighed by the positives. Our room was not damp, the bathroom has its charm. The hotel was open in the seventies I read somewhere, but it has so much character. We arrived at night and were overwhelmed by the charm of the hotel garden, the subtle lighting.The pools, the breakfast were a delight. Sanur is lovely too compared to Nusa Dua where there is nothing to see. Nusa Dua looked like a luxury prison for tourists, It doesn't give you the Balinese feel at all as opposed to Sanur. We explored the rest of the island with a hired car and a driver, cheap and more convenient than bus tours.I would go back in the morning, it was a very special holiday and the Bali Hyatt contributed to that. It is true that you will have to say good morning a few times on the way to breakfast but everyone looks so sincere, you won't mind at all. They make a lot of efforts to make your stay a special one. We received a voucher to use on our last night, a free dinner accompanied by a traditional dance. A nice touch.

<Author>UKxxxx
<Content>Hyatt Family Delight We normally don鈥檛 write reviews, but because the hotel and restaurant are so good we have been compelled to pen a review.We have just come back from a 10 night stay in the Bali Hyatt in Sanur and had a great time. For us as a family it was the perfect choice, as we like a good hotel on the beach, but with easy walking to shops and restaurants. The hotel had a lovely Balinese feel with a great welcome and a relaxed atmosphere. The reception and Wantilian restaurant were wall-less buildings with cool breezes for ventilation, making it feel less like one of those sterile Western glossy hotels. The staff, and in fact all the Balinese people, were very helpful and friendly. The best bit for us was the room and rate we had. We booked direct over the internet and got a family package. This included:a) 2 rooms adjacent rooms connected by a front porch door. This was really useful as a shoes and bucket area, as well as the security to keep an eye on the kids. We asked for an Ocean view room and both rooms had balconies and great sea views. Ours was a huge double bed, and the kids were 2 singles.b) The air conditioning in the rooms worked well and we noticed there was a dehumidifier in the room. This must have been to address comments made by others regarding mustiness, but to be honest, what do you expect in the tropics.c) Breakfast was included. It was buffet style with fruit, bread, cakes, Indonesian dishes, waffles, pancakes, and omelettes cooked to order. A great start to the day.d) A voucher for 1 day during the holiday for both kids to go to their kids club, Camp Sanur.e) And the price? 1,545,775 Rupiah per night for 2 rooms, including the tax. As the quote was in US Dollars, and the pound was strong, this worked out at about 85 GB Pounds per night for the 2 rooms. The other facilities were good too. Tennis, including cheap lessons, on 2 clay courts. There was also a badminton court and a single hole pitch and putt which was free. The 2 table tennis tables were free but busy.In the current climate we have to mention security. All the Balinese we met were Hindu and they really don鈥檛 understand what the Terrorists are trying to achieve. We were slightly concerned before we went out, but these fears were unfounded. We did take sensible precautions with our day trips by getting cars with a driver and guide organised by the hotel. It may have been slightly more but at 45,000 Rupiah for the whole day to where ever you want to go, it is only about 25 GBP. The hotel also has security guards at the gate and on both sides of the beach, which meant you did not get hassled by hawkers!There is a free shuttle to its sister hotel in Nusa Dua. This was nice for a different day as it had bigger pools and a small water slide for the kids, but not the same character. Nusa Dua was a complex of hotels, with a shops and restaurants a long way away.One of the main things we like doing on our holidays is walking and trying out different restaurants each night. Well we found such a great restaurant on day one we kept going back (we did try a couple of others but this was clearly the best). It was the Coriander Restaurant and Bar, 188 Jalan Danau Tamblingan. You turn right outside the hotel and is a 5 minutes walk. The food quality was good, service fast, wide choice and a cheap price. We got welcomed each night with free complimentary cocktail shorts, fried peanuts to nibble on, and a nice fresh piece each of garlic bread. The menu had Western, Italian, Chinese food and local Indonesian favourites. The kids said the fish and chips were the best they ever had, the spaghetti carbonara was lovely and the portions were large. The Indonesian favourites, all very good, were only 1 to 2 GBP! I pushed the boat out one night and had chilli crabs for about 4 GBP! They also do great cocktails. The Pina Colada came in a hollowed out pineapple. So do go to the CORIANDER Restaurant and Bar! We have to mention our daughter Charlotte for picking it. She liked the look of the fresh fish and prawns on display. Charles, Sandy, Charlotte (aged 8) and James (aged 6)

<Author>GeordieLass19
<Content>A very relaxing stay We stayed at Bali Hyatt for 10 nights during a 3 week tour of the Far East. I was a bit concerned after reading some of the negative reviews but glad we chose this hotel. As our room was not ready for us, we were shown to another room and told we could use all the amenities until our room was ready. We eventually went to our allocated Ocean View room which did smell very damp/fusty. I followed the advice of one Tripadviser member and left the wardrobe door ajar when we were in the room to give the aircon unit a chance to dissipate the smell. The tip worked and the smell soon disappeared. We repeated this tip every time we returned to the room and it was not a problem. There were certainly no effects of dampness in the room which was serviced twice a day and left spotless. The bathroom was very dated and rather small, but was spotless and had its own character. The hotel has 3 blocks of rooms and our room was the furthest away from the amenities, but this gave us the perfect chance to say good morning/evening/night about 10 times per journey to the very friendly staff. The beach, however, was reached within a minute. A lovely beach, the staff work very hard to clear it of any seaweed and other stuff that the tide brings in with it once a day. The gardens are magnificent and the two pools very inviting. The pool with the pool bar is very cold - be warned!! Breakfasts were a veritable banquet and the staff very pleasant and attentive. We ate breakfast at the hotel, skipped lunch (breakfast saw us through to the evening) and ate our evening meals in Sanur. Loads of restaurants to choose from and all extremely cheap. Food was very tasty and service excellent. Sanur was very quiet (some call it S'nore) but it suited us down to the ground.We hired a driver/guide and took three full day trips around Bali. We chose to avoid overly touristy places and, in an effort to avoid hawkers, asked to see quieter alternatives. The drive to the central mountain region/rice terraces/temples was very beautiful. We also saw Mounts Agung and Gunung, temples and palaces, and drove to the Eastern parts of Bali. There is so much to see and do you are spoiled for choice, but do some research first so that you can choose what you want to do. In summary, any negatives at Bali Hyatt are vastly outweighed by the positives. The rooms are spotless, the staff extremely helpful and friendly and the breakfasts superb. The pools are excellent, the beach relaxing and the gardens magnificent. We would certainly stay at Bali Hyatt again.

<Content>Bali Hyatt - we loved it Me and my boyfriend together with friends (2 adults + 2children) spent 10days in Bali this June , 6 nights at Bali Hyatt and 4 nights at Nusa Dua Beach Hotel and we were very pleased.I would say rooms at Bali Hyatt (we stayed in the ordinary oceanviewrooms, our friends had 2 rooms with a connecting door ) are good 4 star standard, nicely furnished, a good-size balcony but the bathrooms even though charming in a way are a bit dated BUT the servicelevel and the friendliness of the staff was the very best ! There was lots of staff, when having breakfast for example there was always someone close by to pick-up the empty plate or to bring extra coffee or whatever you required. Always a smile and questions about how you were doing etc. They really made us feel at home from day1.The beach is nice BUT there is lots of seaweed in the water which makes it difficult to swim at low tide. The hotel has 2 pools, both very nice.Apart from breakfast we had just one lunch and one dinner at the hotel. The food and service was excellent but a bit expensive. There is a good choice of restaurants and shops in the Sanur area and if You want to go somewhere else fo shopping  food Kuta is only about 30 minutes away and transportation is easy to find and cheap - we paid about IDR70.000 one-way for a big car (room enough for the 6 of us).One night we went to Jimbaran for seafood; food was excellent and it was a lovely experience to sit directly on the beach and have dinner. The smoke from the restaurants was a bit annoying however. All and all we were very happy with our stay at the Bali Hyatt, Sanur and if I come back I would definitely stay there again

<Author>POKAIMOANA
<Content>Magical Hyatt We have just returned from our holiday at the Bali Hyatt and it was a holiday to remember. It started off with us arriving at the Bali Hyatt gates welcomed by two security guards doing a routined check of the vehicle because of the bombing that had happened. At first I thought that it was a bit intimidating but than understood and appreciated their reasons to keep their guests safe.As the routine ended we then proceeded towards the entrance way of the Hyatt and was welcomed with another warm greeting from the young ladies at the entrance and then got 'laid' (they put over us a lei made out of the flower fragipani, which is a very beautiful smell). Our luggage was taken from our vehicle and we were taken to the foyer. In the foyer we were greeted with two men playing a welcoming song on the Balinese instruments. So straight away we felt like we were in a very magical resort with out even seeing the whole of the resort. With the music playing we proceeded towards the reception. The young lady showed us our seats and we were given a nice cold pineapple and coconut drink served in an actual pineapple with ice and a cold face cloth to cool us down with. All this has happened with out us even checking in yet. Allowing us to drink our drinks and cool down a bit after an eleven hour plane ride the receptionist came and greeted us and checked us in.The staff are very friendly, well spoken and helpful. I had brought with me from home a few electrical appliances, camera, video camera cell phones etc... and the first adapter that was given to me didn't seem to work properly, so I rang the reception and he had a gentelman come to our room to see if he could help me out. He couldn't succeed so he rang an electrician. The electrician was there in a flash and fixed the problem. The staff there go that extra mile to please the customer which made our holiday even better.We stayed in the ocean view room and reading a few of the reviews on this site I feel that the people who say that the rooms are not to their standards must be a very high maintenance type of people and have to remember that you are in Bali, not Hawaii or Rarotonga where the economy there is higher than Bali. You can't tell me you went there because of the sun and surf, you went there because Bali is an affordable island we you get more than your monies worth.The Bali Hyatt is a very beautiful resort to stay at, and my partner and I are already planning a re-visit back there.Cheers guys,Me.

<Author>Dierregi
<Content>Magic , relaxed atmosphere I stayed for the first time at the Bali Hyatt in May 2007, and I very much hope I will go back some days. This was my first trip to Bali, so I read a billion hotel reviews on this site, before chosing the Hyatt. My husband and I were a bit concerned about the negative ones, but we decided to give it a try.On the minus side: the beach is not great, due to the tide. That's it. Everything else we loved. It is indeed a rather old building and the bathrooms really look straight out of the 70's (the garish tiles, the fittings...), however, there is plenty of storage space for toiletries (I always carry a ton) and everything works fine.As far as the dampness mentioned by somebody is concerned, in case you did not notice Bali is a tropical country, subject to hot and humid weather. If you don't like hot and humid, stay in Europe, or wherever you come from. We did not have any dampness-related problem of any kind, our sheets were dry and clean and the room did not have any nasty smell of any kind.The restaurants offer a great variety of good food, the gardens are just fantastic and the pools are great. The green pool is faboulous exactly because it does not have the usual, boring, cold, aseptic blue tiles of most pools. The water is perfectly clean and the colour is due to the material used to build the pool, not to any dirt or mud floating around.The staff is fantastic, very helpful an friendly and the spa is an unmissable experience. You also have the chance to visit the newer Hyatt in Nusa Dua, thanks to the free shuttle service provided. It is a question of personal taste, but if you prefer aseptic and fake minimalistic, you will probably go for the Nusa Dua hotel.The other great advantage of the Bali Hyatt is that it is situated close to shopping and restaurants, so you don't feel like you're prisoner in a golden, tourist cage. The only reason I am not rating this hotel a 5, is because of the bathrooms, otherwise, everything else was just about perfect. Final word: last year we spent our holiday in an all-inclusive, five star Riu hotel in Cabo San Lucas. It was a brand new building, in a semi-desertic environment (dry heat), but we had a lot more problems than in Bali (sewage smell, bad food, staff not so helpful, etc...). So, I decided to rule out forever all-inclusive and go for something different.In the end, it is a matter of taste and of what you are looking for. If you want a magic atmosphere, good service, and stylish surroundings, then this hotel is perfect.  
<Date>May 23, 2007

<Author>Degas
<Content>Living in the past... We first stayed here some 20 years ago and liked it so much we returned 5 years later. So going back after a 15 year gap and after reading the range of reviews I did have some concerns.One of the main plus items on the original trips were the gardens and if anything they have got better and better - if you are a tropical plant fan - you can spend hours just wondering around the grounds.I can't remember any issues with the rooms first time round - but had booked a regency club room to add a little luxury as we are a lot older and fussier then we used to be...... we were disappointed with the room - fittings a little faded, but the main problem was the size- its been a while since I have seen such a small room. As this was a special trip for us we managed to negotiate an upgrade to a great suite for a reasonable extra payment. It was a case of ridiculous to sublime with regards to size as the new suite (?Legong Suite) was a two floor monster with internal staircase and massive walk in wardrobe / bathroom. It also had enormous outside balconies on both floors - with an external shower as well. Too much really - but what the hell! The actual Regency clubroom is in a balinese style open pavillion and is great - complementary breakfast and evening cocktails with daily papers downloaded from the internet. Service through out the hotel was good - apart from one scary lady at the Spa reception.We had several spa sessions and found both the ambiance of the open treatment rooms and the quality of the treatments excellent.Its difficult to sum up overall impressions - the hotel has obviously seen better days - and has been eclipsed by the newer and plusher late comers- but it still has charm and the surroundings and staff make it a good and relaxing way to spend time by the sea in Sanur.
