<Author>John67-7
<Content>Love/Hate  The Bali Hyatt is one of our favourite relaxation holiday destinations in the region. Although there are many newer and better appointed places in Bali, the Sanur Hyatt oozes a kind of charm and relaxed atmosphere that's hard to find elsewhere. The hotel itself is not up today's standards, even if it was award winning in its day, but what it lacks in space, modern amenities, chrome and marble it more than makes up for in design character, privacy and peace by being surrounded by an outstanding mature tropical garden and a private beach. The staff are very friendly and will do almost anything for you (small tips go a very long way here). The Regency Club offers good value and is well worth the small price premium. The real downside is the age of the hotel: in truth the place needs renovating with some rooms now being damp (our room had a separate dehumidifier which more than took care of the problem - I'd strongly recommend you are supplied with one of these if you stay). The food is good with Pizza Ria serving surprisingly accomplished Italian food by the beach.I wouldn't recommend this hotel if you are travelling for business, want nightlife or high degrees of luxury but I believe you will enjoy this hotel if you are seeking a relaxing, quiet and peaceful break and/or are over gleaming edifices and infinity pools. The overall experience is like staying in a small Balinese village with air-con, a gym and room service. It's so relaxing.

<Author>blackfenboy
<Content>Love hate relationship I have stayed at this hotel 5 times over several years. We go to Bali nearly every year and spend two or three days at the Hyatt Sanur to get our bearings and settle into the place. In many respects this hotel is a shocker, but I kind of like it regardless. The lobby is spectacular. The gardens are great. The staff are - for the most part - very friendly and responsive, but often have no idea what you are saying and get requests mixed up. Breakfast was thrown in with our package and so we ate up big (and it is generous and quite good)but went elsewhere for other meals.Rooms are dated, damp and pretty miserable, and only just make acceptable grade. They have improved the Internet service in the basement room below the foyer (which I complained about in a previous post), but have trebled the price. So, I used an Internet cafe - an annoying 10 minute walk away. Before leaving Australia, I sent the hotel two emails seeking information about Internet and other matters, but clearly they got confused. The first response didn't make sense and I didn't get any reply to my second missive. Perhaps I should not care, but they had no idea that I had stayed there before and that my wife had stayed there many more times than me. However, despite everything, the Hyatt Sanur still has a certain charm and appeal. It is actually very difficult to explain, but I suspect some people who have stayed there a few times will know what I mean. And it's good value for money.A lot of people used to Hyatt standards elsewhere, particularly corporates, will be very disappointed by this hotel. The more laid-back traveller will find some goodness and appeal, especially as it is - as I said - pretty good value for money and well situated.Overall, however, I would downgrade this hotel 1/2 point on my previous visit 15 months ago. Incidentally the new -ish security at the hotel entrance- post Bali bombings is ridiculous and superficial compared with some of the other hotels we checked out where the security was, by comparison, real and efficient.Will I stay there again? That's a hard one. I feel like punishing them after some of their dopey behaviour this time round. But , like smoking, it is a bit of weird habit which is hard to shake off.  
<Date>Dec 13, 2006

<Author>gmw2
<Content>Beautiful!! We stayed at the Bali Hyatt for 4 nights which wasn't long enough!! The hotel is set in beautiful grounds. It is deceptively big tho you don't notice unless you walk around. There are 2 pools, with plenty of sun loungers in full sun or shaded areas. Breakfast is lovely with plenty to choose from so its definately worth going bed and breakfast. There are a few other restaurants on site which are a bit pricey but the food is nice. The only slight downside was the dampness in the rooms. We had read about this from other trip advisors so weren't too surprised. There was a dehumidifer in the room but it filled up quickly. As long as it was emptied the damp smell didn't appear. But it wasn't a major issue. The beds are enormous and very comfortable. Our room had a garden view. We were able to sit on the balcony in the evening and listen to mellow jazz from the piano bar. Very civilised!! There are restaurants not far from the hotel serving a wide variety of food at very good prices. Not as nice as the Hyatt but ok! We also found an extremely reasonable laundrette close to the hotel that did a massive load of washing for around 拢3. There isn't alot in Sanur except tourist shops all selling the same thing! You really need to barter for things and they follow you around like your shadow but we got the impression business was really slow so they want a sale!Overall, The Hyatt was lovely, we will definately be back, next time for a lot longer. Enjoy!

<Author>truckeruk
<Content>never a 4*+ hotel booked this hotel through trailfinders in the uk where it was advertised as 4*plus. this is definitely NOT the case !!!The hotel is more like your average 3* med hotel - dated, rooms that smell of damp and bathrooms straight out of the 70's. we asked to be moved as ours has a chipped bath, blood on the wall from what appeared to be a swatted mossie, pillows wet with damp, this damp seeped into everything. Give them their due, upon complaining we were swiftly seen by the general manager and his assistant, who arranged to move, in fact, upgrade us to a better room, offered a free meal (will get to the reason for that in a sec) and joint spa treatment (sheer heaven...) and without any arguement. Going back to the reason for the free feed - well, one of us is veggie, the other omnivore - one of the reasons for choosing this hotel was the fact that it offered no less than 5 restaurants of varying cuisines. Oh goody, no prob with food then...but aarrgh!! On our first night there were only 3 open, none of which had any veggie fare. Guests were expected tp take up the 'cultural evening' offer, ie, the usual abysmal show and buffet slop (again no veggie ). We ended up traipsing forlornly back to our damp, mossie splattered room where we sadly ordered room service. This was why we had the free meal one of the following evenings. On the plus side, the staff are wonderful, the grounds are superb and the spa is fantastic. However, one of the pools resembled a pond - all green (yes, green) and murkey) and a good clean wouldnt have gone amiss. The beach is not the greatest...when the tide is out you can walk out for about half a mile and you will still have the water lapping around your ankles, okay, calves if you are very tall, seaweedy and not great for swimming at any time. In fact, we rarely saw anyone in the sea. If you are looking for a quiet break, not fussy about your room, and like the smell of damp then this is the ideal place.

<Author>TheMaccas
<Content>Fantastic holiday in paradise! Just got back from the most amazing time ever in beatiful Bali. We stayed at the Bali Hyatt for a total of 11 nights. The only bad thing to say that it was not long enough and we really didn't want to come home! A lot of the reviews we read before we booked referred to the hotel as a bit dated. Having stayed at and experienced some of the best hotels in the world, there was simply nothing bad at all about this hotel. Our room was very spacious with a lovely marble bathroom complete with bath and seperate shower. We had a garden room which had a lovely view and was very private. The staff were amazing, so friendly and always has a smile on their face. From manager to cleaner to maintenance guy, everyone took time to greet you and say helo every time they passed you in the hotel. All the facilities were excellent. The pools were very clean, most of the time quiet and very exotic. The gardens were so lush and the lobby and main bar area very relaxing. Food was delicious and although a meal tended to be less expensive in one of the many restaurants in the town, it was still very reasonably priced (evening meal for 2 with a bottle of wine in hotel cost aprox 拢25). We also had time to try the spa facilities which were top class and once again very reasonably priced. Sanur town is aprox 30 mins from the airport and will cost about 拢4.50 in a metred taxi so don't bother with a transfer if you want to save more money. There were plenty of good restaurants and bars along the main strip in Sanur, with Cafe Jepun and The Village being particularly excellent. If you are thinking of hiring a car then ensure you take an international driving licence as we were refused a tourist licence by the police, but be prepared as driving in Bali is among the craziest we've ever come accross, with hardly any road signs just to make it even more difficult. We hired a driver in the end which cost us 拢20 for ten hours driving anywhere you like! All in all, bali was excellent and if you want a little piece of paradise where everyone has a smile on their face then look no further.Ciaran  Vicki (Reading)

<Author>Davey83
<Content>Bali Hyatt - Could be anywhere in the world On arrival at the hotel the staff were very friendly. However, the hotel lacks any sense of Balinese culture and any traveller coming from Europe will find they have travelled a long way to be somewhere that they could have found very much nearer home. Despite travelling in october there were lots of children at the hotel, and the Bali Hyatt is by no means a relaxing option. I am glad I was not on a honeymoon or I would have been very disppointed. Many people writing seem to have stayed in the Regency rooms, which are indeed very much more private, but you pay for that privalege and unless you do that I would not recommend this hotel.One thing that got extremely noticable with the Bali Hyatt was the prices charged by the hotel. Most drinks were over 5 times as much as you could pay if you walked down the road to a local shop, and the essence of this hotel is money money money, virtually nothing is included. Even taxi prices get hiked up for the privalege of them ordering it for you. Bali hyatt prices were very similar to that of UK hotels, a far cry from what you read in the guide books.Despite this it is a nice hotel with lovely gardens, it is just not somewhere that I would advise any European jet setter to go to, bear in mind this hotel is catering for Australian's who see Bali as the UK sees the Spanish Costa's. There are beautiful hotels nearby that appear to retain far more Balinese culture than the Bali Hyatt, which has none.

<Author>Henkybaby
<Content>Very good, but not great I have stayed in many hotels in Sanur. I like Sanur. It is a perfect place to relax outside of the hustle and bustle of Bali. A nice street with lots of hotels and good restaurants. Previous holidays I choose the Puri and Griya Santrian. The first because of the reviews, the second because of the price and location.This time the Hyatt. I remembered it was in the middle of Sanur, so you could easily walk to either side of the town. It's about a 5 to 10 minute walk either way. Nothing is really happening directly outside of the hotel. The hotel has 2 swimming pools, but neither really felt fantastic. The grounds are very large and well kept. Pool area is nice with only a few deck chair battles. Plenty of sun, plenty of shade. The pool bar and restaurant are great and the food and drinks are recommended. At night the main restaurant is not particulary cosy. The food is great, but for a romantic dinner, flee elsewhere. Breakfast deserves a special mention. Probably the best I have had on all my travels. Impressive. If only they would just serve the tea and coffee a little quicker. But truly a great start of the day!!The rooms are good. I had a garden view room (you only spent the night in your room, so a sea view doesn't contribute anything in my belief) which is fine. Nice large bed, nice bathroom (in need of some small maintenance), nice balcony and a TV with lots of channels (also English). Great Internet services at a whopping $12,50 a day (or less if you only check your mail), which is expensive to Balines standards. I use whopping with a smile however. Great value for a fast wireless connection.Staff and service were great. I really need to mention the Spa. A real spa where they give you a real facial, not just a couple of masks and a massage. No: they got the works. It is prices in dollars and a facial is $65. Again, expensive for Bali, but worth it. All in all a nice experience, but not great because the overall feel of the hotel grounds (pool area especially) did not impress. maybe I expected something like the Grand Bali Hyatt... I would recommend this hotel for a stay in Sanur, closely followed by the Puri Santrian, which looses on business services and the fact they have no TV with satellite channels (I travel alone and every once in a while I like my TV).

<Author>persson28
<Content>Typical Package Tour Hotel Hyatt Bali is your typical package holiday hotel. It is not personal, it is not exclusive, it is not luxurious , but it is pleasant and satisfactory. There are no personal touches and you are just one of the hundred guests that come and go. That said it is value for money and has beautiful gardens. The rooms are old fashioned and our air conditioning only managed to cool the room slightly. The staff are generally nice, but as far as I have seen that is a valid statement for most Balinese people who are remarkably gratious. We stayed in Kajane Mua in Ubud prior to Hyatt and the level of service was incomparable. Kajane Mua tried everything possible to make our stay a memorable one and they did. Can't say the same for Hyatt.Hyatt is good as it is affordable and pleasant. As long as you are not looking for exclusive service...

<Author>YaseminOkur
<Content>Your Money Is Worth More Than This In Asia!!! A POOR EXPERIENCEYasemin Okur, SingaporeI travel a lot in Asia for both business and leisure purposes and I work in the service sector to count myself as a seasoned traveller to make the following comments on Bali Hyatt.This is my first ever attempt to write a review in Tripadvisor. The reason of this attempt is that I believe this hotel is overrated and I would like to provide a perspective.This has been the most disappointing stay I had so far in Asia.I do mention Asia , because wherever you go in Asia (especially if you are a westerner), you will be amazed by the quality of service and the beautyluxury of resorts anyway.Here is a quick list why I will never stay in this hotel again:1- The rooms are worn out. They must be sometime from 80's, have not gone under a major renovation ever since. A serious implication of this is the humidity inside the room.2- There is a serious hygiene problem inside the hotel, especially in the common toilets. I had two extremely disappointing experiences, just in 3 days. In the first one, I had to find out myself that all of the toilets by the poolside was blocked. As the hotel staff did not bother to put a notice at the entry, it took me 3 closets with disgusting scenes in each to realize this.Not finished. How can a toilet be filthy at 7.30 am in the morning? The toilets in the main lobby, although it was morning, was not clean at all, the baskets were full of toilet papers, floors were dirty. Smth more like a public toilet in a city center.3- Breakfast is very average, for which hotel charges a surprising 15USD/person. IT IS NOT WORTH IT!!! The variety of food is quite limited, the service is slow due to limited number of staff. Most of the time you end up waiting for a table. The ambience, if you can manage to grab the limited 5 tables by the garden, is OK, otherwise, it is chlostrophobic and dark.4- Pool is not clean. You end up swimming with unknown objects (though some you recognize, such as human saliva) in the smaller pool.Rooms, cleanliness, food and pool. These are for me the key drivers of my hotel choice and the Bali Hyatt scores poorly in each.There are some minor points also such as the inconveniently located amenities, charging for the bikes (most resorts don't expect to profit from this minor service), etc...If this is your first experience in Asia, you may end up rating the hotel more than it deserves.Otherwise, the hotel well deserves a poor rating. I strongly recommend visiting another resort.

<Author>TourGuideBarbie2
<Content>..I miss it already!!!! We arrived in Bali having flown via Kualar Lumpur. It was a long flight but if you fly with a good airline they do all they can to make it bearable!We were supposed to go to Bali for our honeymoon but could not due to the close timing of the incident in Kuta. However, I was kind of glad we didn't as we had the most incredible trip in the end, which I doubt nowhere could match....However, Bali is an amzaing place, inexpensive, safe, friendly, beautiful, but the hotel was albeit very nice and the gardens superb. I found the rooms to be a little old particularilly the bathroom! However, this was in some way made up by having a room with a balcony over the regency lounge where live balineese music would be played in the evening..magical! The pools were lovely, but felt due to the surrounding trees and flowers the 'green' pool could have been cleaned more often throughout the day. The overall design of the gardens and pool were wonderful, and the beach (at high tide) is lovely, but low tide is not a post card pitcure. Although you can see the most sacred mountain from the beach. when the tide is out you can walk out into the weeds and see the largest star fish I have ever seen...up to 30cm in diameter! There did not appear to be anything nasty in the seaweed, but would suggest wearing rubber shoes if you want to go out far!!!The hyatt had a lovely reception, greeting you with flowers, music and a cold drink. The breakfast buffet was great and we looked forward to the fresh fruit and pastries daily. However, the price of food and drink in the hotel was outrageous. We did not eat once there for dinner. There are so many very nice restaraunts in Sanur. Recommend Ming  The Village I was amazed that these restaraunts managed to produce western food to a high standards, but of course their own cuisine was excellent too, but sometines you get a little fed up with the hot stuff. The fish in and around Bali is the best, exquisitte and would also recomment The Wantillian on the beach, walk along the beach path (left out ot the hyatt) anfd you will find tables on the sand, live music and the fish caught that day on the menu.....lovely.We did not explore enough of Bali, and do want to return. I would go back to the Hyatt as sanur has a good balance in terms of tourists etc...the Hyatt is supposed to be the best hotel in Sanur and we certaily did not see any other to question that. Taxis are very cheap...you have 2 kinds one is a van with bench seats which are very cheap, but would only use those to go up and down Sanur. Otherwise the taxis are good and also inexpensive we went to Kuta 3 or 4 times at a cost of 40,000 rupiah (about 拢2.50) each way.Bali is safe enough to travel around without a guide, the people are so spiritually guided they dare not commit crime nor offend anyone, quite a change from most places in the world. Avoid going with the fixed tour agent tour, unless you are prepared to only be taken to pre-arranged shops etc where pricres are far higher (due to intro commissions etc)Bali is fabulous and have never felt so much at peace, and this is down to the kindness of it's people...you must go! the temples are like nothing I have ever seen......I have got to go back and explore the west!

<Author>mdkate1657
<Content>Great facilities disappointing rooms We stayed at the Bali Hyatt for 7 nights as part of a three week honeymoon in Singapore and Bali. The welcome we received was great with a cool drink and flower garland. Our initial impression of the hotel was good.We loved the facilities this hotel had - great pools, restaurants, gardens, service etc. These are all more recent additions to the hotel. This hotel has one big failing which you can not get away from - the bedrooms!When we were shown the bedroom we were deeply disappointed, they were certainly not the standard we were expecting from a four star Hyatt hotel.The accommodation blocks are outdated 1970's concrete or nuclear bunkers as my husband referred to them. Much as they are attempted to be disguised by greenery, they are still visible.The bedrooms and small, cramped, smelt of damp with dark dingy bathrooms. We asked to move from our beach view room - so far away from the beach, the sea was barely visible. We had booked a Regency room but this certainly was not one. We were moved to a garden view Regency room which was slightly better. The bathroom was lighter and more airy but the bedroom itself even smaller as part of it had been taken up by the larger bathroom. It was still not what we would expect from a 4* Hyatt hotel.Bedrooms aside we really enjoyed our stay. Breakfast was good. We ate meals both at the hotel, very good quality and reasonably priced, and outside the hotel. Local restaurants were very good quality and very cheap. Would I recommend this hotel? I don't know! Aside from the rooms this hotel was great. I don't know what could be done to improve the rooms as even if modernised they would still be small. My advice - go to Sanur, great restaurants, bars etc BUT find a hotel with better bedrooms, especially if it is your honeymoon, as these do not have that special touch we had at our hotels to make your honeymoon that bit more special and memorable.

<Author>gimjam
<Content>anniversary heaven my wife and i have just returned from an eight night stay at the bali hyatt .The trip was to celebrate our twentieth wedding annivrsary and it was absolutely fantastic. We stayed in a Regency club room which entitles you to continental breakfast in the club lounge and complimentary drinks (alcoholic and non alcoholic cocktails) between 5pm and 7pm, tea and coffee is available free all day. The hotel is set in the most amazing gardens and all the staff from reception right through to the gardeners are polite and they make you feel special and extremly welcome.We never noticed any smell in our room a problem that some say they have experienced. Although the beach is a lovely place to relax its not really a swimmers beach as it is protected by a coral reef and is tidal, the two combining to make the water only really deep enough for a bathe.The four restaurants offered good and varied menus but for a true taste of bali you should venture out of the hotel to one of the local restaurants where the food was not only better but nearly half the price. All in all it was a tremendous way to spend our anniversary and we look forward to returning to bali and the bali hyatt in the very near future.

<Author>therobster
<Content>Best service in Asia My wife and I went on our honeymoon to Bali and stayed both at the Bali Hyatt and the Bali Ritz-Carlton. The Hyatt was fantastic, the Ritz-Carlton terrible. Upon arrival at the Bali Hyatt you are greeted by genuinely friendly staff. They come across as 'real people' rather than people who have just been trained to cater to you - and this means you get the friendliest, most efficient service I've experienced almost anywhere throughout your stay. The hotel itself is set in a huge garden that contains a great variety of plants (and birds! we were surprised by an owl coming straight at us on the first night :) fortunately it was more scared of us than we were of it). The architecture is 70s concrete - but it is covered by vines and plants which softens it immensely, so you feel much more like you're in a garden than a hotel. Rooms can feel a bit damp if you don't have your air-conditioning on - but there's little reason not to.There are 4 or so restaurants at the hotel, all of which served great food. We're pretty fussy about our food, which doesn't mean we expect haute cuisine at every meal, just insist on getting the basics right. So if you order a steak sandwich at the poolside, it should come pretty quickly and be tender steak, served with a genuine smile, right? Right. At the Bali Hyatt they do this kind of thing naturally. At the Ritz, we found out this kind of stuff was beyond them, and at twice the price. Go figure.We were due to spend 5 days at the Hyatt, then 5 days at the Ritz. After staying at the Ritz for one night we couldn't stand it any longer and went straight back to the Hyatt. We loved it.  
<Date>Oct 8, 2006

<Author>jackieboo
<Content>Perfect holiday We arrived at the Hyatt after a total journey of approx 24 hours to be met with smiles, flower garlands, a refreshing cool drink and cool towels. They also took our photo (after that long a journey what did we look like!!!). Our ocean view Regency Club room was not quite ready so they gave us a temporary room for a couple of hours. When we did arrive in our room it was wonderful with brilliant sea views. The Regency Club was worth the extra cost, if only for the peace and tranquility it provided. It was so relaxing to have breakfast in there and complementary early evening drinks with finger foods. The staff address you by name and are so attentive without being in your face. The whole of the Bali Hyatt was beautiful. The grounds are kept immaculate and so beautiful. We ate in the Italian Restaurant next to the beach and also the restaurant next to the pool (sorry cannot remember their names), both were very good. Drinks in the Hyatt are cheaper than at home but are more expensive than out in Sanur or around Bali. The Bali Hyatt is also in a very good position in Sanur, with shops, bars and restaurants on either side of its entrance but far enough away not to cause a disturbance.Shortly after our arrival we had a jet lag massage int he hotel spa. It was quite expensive but worth every penny - we slept like babies that night. We had booked this before our arrival at the Hyatt. We hired a driver recommended by a friend and he was amazing . We went out with him for 3 full days and we saw the real Bali. He speaks perfect English and my husband and he were great mates by the end of the first day talking about rock music whilst travelling around Bali. On another day we went to the far north of Bali to see the little girl that we sponsor - what an emotional experience that was but very rewarding.Sanur is a very good place to stay. It is not as hectic as Kuta but there are still lot and lots of restaurants and bars along the main street. There is also the beach path which runs the length of Sanur, just be aware of the sellers that follow you. There are no time share touts as there are in Kuta.All in all we had a brilliant holiday and cannot wait until we can return, hope fully not in the too distant future. We would definite stay at the Bali Hyatt again.  
<Date>Aug 25, 2006

<Content>Overhyped and utterly disappointing. Please do not waste your money I took my parents to a 4D 3N vacation in Bali in May 2006 and we stayed in Bali Hyatt. I totally regret having chosen Bali Hyatt as our hotel for the trip. We paid exhorbitant price to stay here, only to find that nothing except the gardens was worth it.The so called garden-view rooms had a damp and old feel, the room-decor was neither traditional nor modern, the taps in the bathroom leaked, the bathrooms had awfully dingy walls painted in green and a cracked bath-tub, the metallic springs in the bed mattress hurt the back and there was no internet connection.The hotel is also too big and not designed for easy access to most frequented areas such as the main lobby, the pools and the restaurants. As a result, you have to walk excessively everytime you get out of your room. The corridors you walk thorugh are not well-lit at night and on the whole, it feels you are living in some cheap student hostel till you reach the lobby.I am usually not the complaining types but this time, I really felt cheated to realise that the hotel is simply overhyped.Choose this hotel only if you don't care about money and don't mind the feeling of having been taken for a ride.

<Author>mannio
<Content>Excellent Stay A group of us stayed at the Bali Hyatt in Sanur in December. The hotel was really well run and the service was excellent. I would definitely recommend the upgrade to the Regency club as you get to have breakfast in a extremely peaceful club lounge surrounded by lotus ponds and beautiful gardens. The best bit about it though are the free Gin and tonics and nibbles in the evening which are definitely a good way to start your evening. Service in the Regency club is excellent with all the staff adding a personal touch by referring to you by name. One of our group had a birthday whilst we were there and the staff made a great effort with a cake and singing Happy Birthday. They also took photos of the event and presented these 10 miutes later in Balinese style frames for us to keep. The Chinese restaurant that belongs to the hotel serves lovely food but is quite pricey. The other restaurants in the hotel were also good but there were some very nice restaurants worth trying outside of the hotel. For a cheaper alternative at lunchtime go left out of the back entrance and follow the beach round to the Stiff Chilli (about 5-8min walk) this serves great and extremely cheap authentic Italian pizzas and pastas. We visited Ubud the place famous for the Monkey forest and art galleries, We got a taxi there from Sanur and it was about 拢10 each way. You can buy large modern canvas prints from some of the galleries which are a fraction of the price of those sold in the UK. I would highly reccommend the Green House restaurant if you do take a trip to Ubud, the food was excellent as was the service. We did a day tour of the island which was interesting but we made sure we specified we did not want to stop at craft shops as this is the usual ploy of tour guides. Anyone feeling a bit more energentic that fancies trying their hand at surfing should go to the Ripcurl school of surf, the instructers were enthusiastic and very professional which made the experienc really enjoyable. The spa at the hotel is meant to be excellent but I did not try it. If you want a cheaper alternative then there are plenty of Foot and body massage places in Kuta which only cost about 拢4 for an hour. The staff were all really friendly and it is a great way to pass the time if it's raining, the girls can even get a pedicure or manicure for about 拢4 at these places. Overall I would say Sanur is a lovely place but do get out and venture to Kuta and Ubud for a change in atmosphere. The taxis are so cheap it's worth it.

<Author>Whinbrook
<Content>Mixed Bag Stayed 5 nights in the Bali Hyatt over two visits a few days apart and while a pleasant hotel it is not 5 stars as some would lead you to believe but an average 4 star with some reservations. It is true that the bedroom blocks are ugly but the public areas are authentic Balinese style, and set in beautiful immaculately kept grounds. But, being authentic (and very attractive and characterful) they are all open sided so not air conditioned. During our stay it was very warm and humid and unfortunatley using the public areas was very uncomfortable due to lack of a/c.On both stays we opted for the Regency Club which provided a nice haven (a large thatched Balinese style open area set in a very pretty water garden) to have breakfast, complimentary tea and coffee through out the day and cocktails and snacks in the early evening. However, the rooms disappointed and there appeared to be nothing to set Regency Club rooms apart from the standard rooms. Our first room was cramped and not very comfortable, especially the hard unforgiving small beds. The bathroom was quite luxurious and large in contrast but the towels thin and almost thread bare. Our second room, when we returned having been travelling was larger and had a sea view but the beds were still dreadful and this time the bathroom was in need of a make over. We did not encounter any damps smells on either visit as mentioned in previous reviews.The restaurants were good and we generally enjoyed our meals and had very good and friendly service (all the hotel staff are very pleasnat and friendly and it was a pleasure to have them around). Four of the five eating establishments were open for business but the hotel was very quiet during our stay, certainly under half full. However, while dining in the open air grill one evening a rat ran across the terrace which spoiled the occassion and several very sad looking stray dogs had found their way into the grounds and sat close to our table hoping for a scrap which was upsetting to watch. No staff made any effort to shoo the dogs away (Bali is over run with packs of stray dogs, some very sick looking).The pool area was picturesque and the beach was kept immaculate but swimming in the sea was not very pleasant as the water is very shallow at Sanur due to the off shore reef. Even when the tide was in the water barely came above calf level several hundred feet from the shore. When the tide was out people were walking on the reef itself.We found Sanur not particularly picturesque and in no way did it feel authentic as guide books like to describe, it felt run down and was dirty and infact we thought Bali failed to live up to the hype generally. But it is true the Balinese are extremely nice people, warm and friendly and the crafts available to buy all over the island are fantastic.  
<Date>Dec 2, 2005

<Content>Excellent Hotel and resort We stayed for 14 nights from the 15th October 2005All the positive comments from other reviews are absolutley true.All the Balinese people we met both within the hotel or outside were very friendly and helpful.There are many bars and restaurants within easy walking distance of the hotel ( either right or left ) . <Author>missced
<Content>Paradise. Fantastic, and excellent service We stayed at the Bali Hyatt for five nights in October 2005 as part of a SE Asia tour organised by Kuoni, only four days after the most recent bombings. I cannot speak highly enough of the staff and standard of service at the hotel. Given that it was a difficult time for all concerned, our concerns were laid to rest as soon as we arrived - the hotel complex itself is very well guarded, and incoming and outgoing traffic is searched. And terrorism is terrorism all over the world - we live in London, and our experience at the Bali Hyatt has reinforced the view that we will not let the terrorists win by spreading fear. The balinese people are highly aesthetic, friendly and welcoming, and were all appalled by the latest events. We were made to feel incredibly welcome, and the standard of service we recieved was second to none.The landscaped gardens are large and beautifully set out in a balinese style, with fragrant ylang ylang, orchids, bougainvillea, etc growing profusely everywhere. Sanur beach is wonderful - the tide goes out quite far once a day, with plenty of exotic sea life to look at. Whilst it is tidal, waves are gentle and not for surfing, as the beach is protected by a coral reef some 400m offshore. It was quite the most unique beach I have been to yet - Crabs, seaweed, sea snails - the place is naturally as near to paradise as I have been, with the added advantage of a secure hotel resort area. There is a long path along the seafront, where we did after a day or two venture to local restuarants. Local fishermen still use the beach with local colourfully painted boats. This is great for peace and quiet and local character - and if you want luxury, it is there aplenty in the hotel. The hotel's public areas are well maintained, with a balinese open style roof by the piano bar. The mixture of the humid climate, fragrant planting of the gardens, layered level gardens,unobtrusive local musicians and landscaped swimming pools all add to the atmosphere. The hotel is large, and three storey, and clearly built in the seventies - but we did not have a issue with this at all as it has been decorated well in a local style, (each courtyard is lit with hangings and teracotta pots at night, the gardens are dotted with lanterns) and the outside is covered in vegetation. Many reviews mention a damp smell - the climate is excessively humid (usually over 80%) and this is the reason for the confusion, I believe. The rooms themselves were not damp, and well maintained. Food in all the restaurants was excellent - and if you wish to venture outside you will find good local food very cheaply. By western standards the Hyatt is not expensive either. A win-win situation!I used the spa, which was first class. If you would like a cheap massage on the beach, fine, but the spa was professional, immaculate, clean and intensely relaxing (I had a massage, and little touches such as having a fragrant wooden bowl of water with flowers floating in it underneath your head as you place your face in the hole in the massasge table) are thoughtful touches which make all the difference. And for a snip of the price at home! Before we went to the Bali Hyatt we were a couple of uncertain tourists, - we moved on to our next destination in love with the place. We would definitely stay at the Bali Hyatt again - the service is superb, and you have the option of going outside the resort if you wish, so how one enjoys the holiday is up to you.  
<Date>Oct 25, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic place dont let the terrorists win From the moment we arrived we received a very warm welcome from the staff in the hotel. We agree with the damp problem in the room, the first room we were allocated had the damp smell so we decided to change rooms. We spoke to the reception who were very accommodating and had no problem in relocating our room. (I鈥檓 sure they are used to it as it does seem to be a problem with many rooms) We decided to upgrade our room to a Regency Club Room with this we also got our breakfast and evening drinks between 5 and 7. We found this was definitely worth the extra cost. (Remember to haggle for a good deal)The hotel and all the facilities were amazing, the only disappointment was the beach, as the other reports say due to the corral reef that is about 100m out to sea the water never gets very deep and you get lots of see weed. Some times if the sea isn鈥檛 rough enough the water on the inside of the reef doesn鈥檛 get changed. This affected us a couple of times when we went scuba diving just up from the hotel. The sand on the beach is swept all the time and is very clean. Sun beds under the beach umbrellas are almost impossible to get some people must get up in the middle of the night to get them. As I mentioned the swimming in the sea was a bit off a disappointment so we spent most of the time around the pools that I have to say are incredible. The gardens/grounds to the hotel are an absolute credit, absolutely beautiful and immaculately kept.If you have some extra cash to spend, we fully recommend going to the hotel spa. We both did a 2 and a half hour package with various treatment and had the best time. The staff made you feel so welcome and special. It鈥檚 a real treat.To sum up we would without a doubt recommend this hotel we had a holiday of a lifetime.One final note, don鈥檛 be put off by the terrorist situation in Bali, we were in Bali at the time of the latest terrorist attacks, apart from heightened security entering the hotels (car and bag checks) Bali is still a paradise island. The Balinese people are the most friendly and good natured people you will come across who are so anti to any type of violence. They are so dependant on tourism as it is their main forms of income, as you can imagine they are very concerned that the attacks are going to prevent travel to Bali.Happy holidays

<Author>nozmeister
<Content>Great holiday, but the hotels needs some attention! We've just returned from two weeks at the Bali Hyatt. We stayed there 5 years ago at about the same time of year and wanted to return as we has such a good time the first time! (even the bombing didn't affect our enjoyment of the island)Basically we had a very enjoyable holiday but whereas the main areas of the hotel are fine and the staff excellant we found that there are a few issues around.- When we arrived we asked for a double room but were given a twin. When we went to ask for a change there were none available until the following night, the following day they then wanted us to move to another room which despite paying for an OceanView we could hardly see the ocean. Eventually we got a room with an ocean view although as it was on the ground floor it wasn't really worth the extra.- The rooms and the bathroom in particular needs a complete refit. This hadn't been changed in the five years since we were last at the resort and we thought that it could do with it then! This makes me wonder about the 4 star rating as this is fine outside the rooms.- They appeared to have a bath towel problem as every day we were left without bath towels and had to ring up for them most nights as they didn't come round to service the rooms again until about 7pm. This is far too late for most people.Having also stayed in Nusa Dua I agree with the other comments that Sanur is a good mix between the buzz of Kuta and the cold could be anywhere in the world feel of Nusa Dua. We went to the Grand Hyatt in Nusa Dua a couple of times when we stayed there and was very quiet due to the renovation work but it does have a very nice pool and the beach is better than in Sanur. Food/drink prices are very high though !!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>great value for money, fantastic We stayed 9 nights at the Bali Hyatt and after reading some of the reviews which were on 'Trip Advisor' we were expecting damp rooms and an out dated hotel. However when we got there we were pleasently surprised. From the moment we arrived with the welcome cocktail and the garland of flowers, the standard was set, and the room was exactly (aircon working fine) like on the brochures and websites! We were there on our honeymoon and were told before we left that we may or may not get an upgrade. We were upgraded to the 'Regency Club' room with a garden view which was perfect for us. Every evening we would be serenaded on our balcony with the balinese music coming from the Regency club lounge and all the tropical sounds of animals in the beautiful gardens. However after a while the music did seem to be a bit repetative and like someone was standing on my cats tail. But it all added to the atmosphere. The staff were extremely friendly. Nothing was too much trouble and always with a pleasent greeting. The breakfast was fantatic we would recommend the pancakes and eggs which are cooked freshly while you wait. The regency club from our opinion is not worth the money though, as it seemed vey quiet (basically only free drinks and exculsive breakfast in the club lounge) The 2 pools and private beach (guarded and cleaned continiously) is more than enough to choose a nice spot for the day, and there is enough watersports to choose from (don't forget to bargain!). You can also get a local massage by the beach for less than 6 usdollars for an hour. This hotel is certainly the best one in Sanur, and we also visited the nusa dua hotels but agree with all reviews that those are very isolated and cold and have no local atmosphere (may as well be anywhere else in the world). Grand hyatt is apparently being renovated (sep 2005) and was less than 30% full so its was extremely quiet as well. One of the only few attractions in nusa dua area is the large shopping mall which was also closed for renovation/construction. All reviews with regards to Kuta/Sanur/Nusa Dua are correct; Kuta is young, cheaper hotels, lots of bars and discos full of Aussies, while Sanur is much more quiet, more Europeans, Japanese and honeymooners. Nusa dua finally is nice and new (mainly Europeans and Japanese) but can imagine it to be quite boring. With regards to the beaches it is true that the tide goes out very far in the afternoon, and that there is relatively lots of seaweed, but simply nature and still good enough for us Europeans! For us we really made the right choice with the Bali Hyatt in Sanur and would recommed it to all! Bargaining in Bali is quite an experience, anywhere outside hotel grounds (like on the 'surfers' Kuta public beach for example where the west coast sunset can be admired) you will constantly be approached to buy something from locals, but still almost always with a smile and relatively civilized still. Some usefull tips: 'Blue bird' taxis are apparently the most reliable ones, one way trip between Sanur and Kuta for example is approx 4 usdollars (through the hotel around 8 usdollars). You can easily book day trips to see more of Bali, highly recommendable. Eating out is easy and highly affordable in Sanur, although hotel does have great restaurants too for relatively reasonable prices still. All in all a great place and people, for an unforgetable honeymoon! Enjoy.  
<Date>Sep 27, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Exceeded expectations We have just returned from a fantastic holiday at the Bali Hyatt in Sanur. The hotel itself is certainly older than most - I understand that it was first opened in 1972 (however, has obviously undergone many renovations which has kept it fresh). Given the age of the hotel, the surrounding gardens are well developed and give it an exceptional ambience (very relaxing!). Out of interest, we visited the Grand Hyatt in Nusa Dua (a shuttle bus runs frequently each day between the 2 hotels) to take a look. The Grand Hyatt is a newer hotel, but to be honest it felt 'cold' and uninviting - a very 'resort' style hotel. Not to mention that there is very little within walking distance of the hotel and the food/ drinks are about 50% more expensive than the Bali Hyatt. Oh yes - and in the interest of supporting my comments that it is very 'resort' style, there is a Marks  Spencer and Starbucks opening up at the resort soon (if you have no interest in Bali or it's culture, this resort is for you).There was a great crowd at the Bali Hyatt - a good mix of people (different cultures, ages). They have a great pool bar and piano bar (live music). The restaurants on site are very good quality at a reasonable price. There is an exceptional chinese restaurant as well. The breakfast (normally included) is the largest I have seen in a hotel - exceptional standard.Try the restaurants outside the hotel - there is a fantastic italian restaurant called 'The Village' - some of the best Italian we have ever had. There are many others great spots in the surrounding area, you just need to have a good look around.I would definately recommend the hotel and the location. Sanur itself has a nice quieter feel than Kuta, and less 'manufactured' than the Nusa Dua area.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Honeymoon trip in Hyatt We stayed in the Bali Hyatt for our honeymoon in August 05 and found it to be a worthwhile experience, with some tips we would like to share. Firstly, the hotel staff are really friendly, we ended up saying good morning, good afternoon and good evening about 40 times a day! But in all fairness they are just lovely people and go out of their way to be nice....The room we stayed in had no dampness or any other problems that previous reviews have mentioned, we found it to be immaculate in every way (it was an oceanview in the Bougainvillea block on the second floor) with great views and it was constantly looked after by the staff i.e. they would ask if we wanted the bed turned down every evening and would do a clean up and refresh of towels etc. of the room if we were not in and so on...The property itself is really lovely, its an ideal location especially for honeymooners who want to relax etc. We travelled to another beach where we were constantly hassled on the beach to buy items etc. and couldn't wait to return to the calmness of our own beach the next day, albeit there are some guys asking if you want to go on jet skis etc. As per other reviews the grounds and pools are spectacular and are very traditionally Balinese. The spa in particular is worth a visit. We really enjoyed the experience. The only thing we found was that after three nights of dining in the hotel restaurants that some of the restaurants outside the complex were worth dining in and are vastly less expensive particularly The Village and Palay and are also equally as good. It is definitely worth the visit. Another thing we found was that the only place you could have a drink in the hotel in the evening was the Piano bar near the lobby which was extremely repetitive after a few nights, i.e. the music was the same and the faces of the guests became familiar.... The entertainment should certainly differ here!!!!Overall we had a fantastic time and would definitely recommend the relaxation and pampering after organising a wedding !!!!Just to add that we went to the Hyatt at the end of August and never found it a problem finding a sunbed or a table at breakfast in the morning, some reviews mention queuing being a problem but we certainly didnt. All in all we had a great experience for 10 nights!! We would definitely recommend it, enjoy !!!!

<Author>yorkieYork_England
<Content>Difficult to fault Having spent nearly two weeks here I find it hard to fault this hotel for all round value for money. Ok, the residential blocks are concrete and of their age, but what do you expect. They are unobtrisive and serve their purpose.We had interconnecting rooms at the far end which suited us fine. Rooms were as we expected with no sign of the smells referred to in other reviews. The balcony was on the small side as rooms were on the top floor. If you want bigger balconies go for a lower floor though that might be at the expense of views. Room service was very prompt and we were looked after very well.Pool areas are first class and, despite being there in peak season there was no problem with sun beds. Pool attendants were happy to find spare beds and move them to where you wanted.All public areas, restaurants and bars are very good, all with a typical Balinese character. with excellent service throughout. Prices are not bad for this standard of hotel although bars and restaurants outside the hotel are much cheaper as you would expect. A meal for 4 in the hotel could cost between 拢20 and 拢30 for four (which isn't bad) whereas outside would cost around 拢15 for four.

<Author>CathBrad
<Content>A real treat! We stayed in the Bali Hyatt for a week and loved every minute!The hotel itself is amazing in our opinion. The service were amazing and the staff couldn't do enough for us. The grounds are lovely with two great pools.The rooms are nice, but yes there is a damp smell. If you go for the regency rooms it costs about 拢10 a night more and you get free drinks from 5-7pm. Well worth it. plus you get breakfast away from the main part which is much more relaxed and no waiting for tables or food.Sanur is nice. The beach is amazing. It is worth taking the free shuttle bus over to the Grand Hyatt as it seems less busy with plenty of choice of sunbeds unlike the Hyatt. Like another review said, people put their towels on sunbeds then go away for hours, but when we mentioned it to staff they said they had a rule if beds are left unattended for more than half an hour, the towels will be taken away. And they did. I saw it on several occasions.Overall a lovely hotel in a great country.
